End of the Rainy Season; Italian Army Awaits Orders to Advance; Troops Gather on Eritrean Border; Rumor of Conflict Between Italian Premier and King Over Territory 64

Djibouti, Asmara (From Our Correspondent): Reports from Asmara state that Italian troops concentrated on the Eritrean border are awaiting orders to advance on Adowa. However, preparations for the offensive are not yet complete. This is evidenced by the continuous movement of troops. It is said that each regular army division is equipped with one division each of Blackshirts and native soldiers, but the latter two divisions are much smaller than the regular army. The Blackshirts are designated as reserves, with the regular army and native soldiers as the vanguard. Among the artillery preparing to bombard Adowa, many 75mm field guns were seized from the Austrian army during the European war. (National Telegram, 24th)

Addis Ababa: The French Embassy requested that the protection of the Djibouti-Addis Ababa railway be entrusted to 180 French soldiers near the Dire Dawa station. It is reported that the Emperor has refused, citing that the railway is not currently in danger. It has not rained in Abyssinia for two days, leading people to believe the rainy season is over. (National Telegram, 24th)

(Paris): Local newspapers believe that Italy's hesitancy to engage in immediate warfare is the result of a conflict between Mussolini and King Emmanuel II. The King reportedly questioned Mussolini whether it was wise to forcibly seize Abyssinia at the risk of world condemnation. According to the "L'Oeuvre" newspaper, Britain anticipates that a "nobleman" will replace Mussolini as Prime Minister. (National Telegram, 24th)

(Rome): The Cabinet today ordered that soldiers serving in East Africa may have proxy marriages performed by agents in their home country. (National Telegram, 24th)

Italian Government Orders Churches in Cities to Black Out During Wartime to Avoid Air Raids 65

(Rome): Today, the Italian government and the Vatican authorities reached an agreement that if enemy aircraft attack Rome, Vatican City will also comply with blackout orders. This compromise is highly valued, as it signifies that the independent Vatican City will stand united with Italy in wartime. Today, the Italian Cabinet approved an allocation of one million lire to build air raid shelters in Messina. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

Marconi Arrives in Brazil to Attend Radio Station Opening Ceremony; Will Stay for a Week Before Departing for Service in East Africa 66

Capital of Brazil: Italian radio inventor Marquis Marconi has arrived here. Representatives from the government, both houses of parliament, and various scientific organizations welcomed him at the pier. The Marquis is here to attend the opening ceremony of a local radio station. He plans to stay for a week before returning to his country and proceeding to serve in East Africa. During his visit here, he will be hosted by the government. (Havas Telegram, 24th)

Widespread Rumors in London That the Abyssinian King Has Issued a Mobilization Order; According to Custom, All Nationals Must Join the Military; Yemeni Immigrants Wish to Serve Abyssinia 67

(London): Conflicting reports arrived here today from Addis Ababa, stating that the Abyssinian King has issued an immediate general mobilization order. It is said that this order was not only signed by the King but also countersigned by Archbishop Abuna. According to Abyssinian custom, after a mobilization order is issued, all nationals capable of bearing arms must immediately join the military. (Reuters Telegram, 25th)

Addis Ababa: A delegation of 150 Yemeni immigrants residing in Abyssinia recently paid homage to the Abyssinian King, expressing their sympathy for Abyssinia's position in the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. They stated their great satisfaction with residing in Abyssinia and their readiness to defend Abyssinian territory, even at the cost of bloodshed. (Havas Telegram, 25th)

Page 8

League of Nations Experts Studying Sanctions Issue Fear U.S. Will Undermine Them 68

(Geneva): The League of Nations' Committee of Five is preparing to halt its mediation efforts. League of Nations experts are now focusing on the possibility that the United States might sell goods to Italy if various countries impose economic sanctions. The experts are deeply concerned about how to legally address the situation if the United States disregards the League of Nations' economic sanctions and sells large quantities of goods like cotton, kerosene, and copper to Italy. The recent U.S. Neutrality Act does not authorize the President to prohibit the export of goods to belligerent nations. Therefore, implementing sanctions against Italy may require undermining Italy's creditworthiness. (National Telegram, 24th)

U.S. Munitions Control Board Holds First Meeting; List of Prohibited Items to Be Submitted to President for Review 69

(Washington): The National Munitions Control Board held its first meeting today, chaired by Secretary of State Hull. Representatives from the Departments of War and Navy and Secretary of Commerce Roper attended. They briefly considered the list of munitions prohibited from being supplied to belligerent nations under the Neutrality Act and approved it. The list has now been submitted to the President for review. The Board is currently unwilling to disclose how the prohibited items are classified in the list. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

(Washington): The National Munitions Control Board has completed a list of "vehicles, munitions, and weapons." In the future, when President Roosevelt issues orders based on the newly passed Neutrality Act, this list will be used as the basis. It is understood that the President will order all manufacturers, producers, and exporters of items on the list who conduct foreign trade in such items to apply for licenses. (National Society Telegram, 24th)

Malta Tests Blackout 70

Last night, the authorities in Malta conducted a blackout test, plunging the entire island into darkness for half an hour. Crowds gathered at convenient locations to watch the test. Streetlights were extinguished first, followed by lights in homes, ships, and cars, all at once. Traffic gradually ceased, and the whole island was pitch black. Simultaneously, aircraft soared overhead. The public responded quickly. Recently, the authorities had announced to residents that in the event of an emergency, all lights must be extinguished. The test last night was to see how quickly the public would comply with the order. (Reuters Telegram, 25th)

Inauguration Ceremony of New Prison in Addis Ababa 71

Capital of Abyssinia: A new prison here was inaugurated yesterday by the Abyssinian Emperor in person. Members of the diplomatic corps were also present. The prison includes a church, a factory, and detailed regulations, strictly protecting animals and prohibiting arbitrary abuse. Abyssinia possesses all the organizations of a civilized nation. (Havas Telegram, 25th)

Greece Discusses National Defense, Passes Important Resolutions to Cope With Future Events 72

Prime Minister Tsaldares of Athens convened a Supreme National Defense Council to discuss the situation in the Mediterranean. It is rumored that several important resolutions were passed, but their content remains secret. It is said that the issues of supplying the army and navy with munitions and plans to prepare submarines, destroyers, and bombers to cope with all eventualities were all included. The Council also shortened the delivery time for munitions from one year to three months. (National Telegram, 25th)

Germany Does Not Want to Be Drawn Into the Italo-Abyssinian Dispute 73

(Berlin): According to sources here, it is anticipated today that Germany will not participate in the European dispute caused by Italy's actions. The German government believes that a strict neutral stance is a natural consequence of improved Anglo-German friendship and that Germany would gain nothing by joining either side. However, by staying out of it, Germany can demonstrate to the world that its approach to European relations is one of peace. Local newspapers believe that Italian newspapers are exaggerating the relationship between Germany and Lithuania in an attempt to divert the attention of Britain and the League of Nations, causing them to slightly forget about Italy's serious situation. (National Telegram, 24th)

Sweden Strictly Adheres to Neutrality; Deeply Concerned About the Situation in Northern and Central Europe 74

Capital of Sweden: Most newspapers here support the proposals put forward by Foreign Minister Sandler at the League of Nations Assembly. All political parties, such as the majority of members of the Conservative Party and the left-wing Social Democrats and trade unionists, believe that participating in sanctions against Italy is extremely dangerous. Therefore, they advocate maintaining strict neutrality in the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. Conservative newspapers believe that Sweden's participation in sanctions, even if they are economic in nature, is fraught with danger. Sweden's concern lies in the increasingly tense situation in Northern Europe, particularly the Memel issue. In the event of an accident, Sweden would have to take military measures against Germany, making it difficult to address the Italo-Abyssinian issue. (Havas Telegram, 25th)

London Financiers Pay Attention to Gold Flowing to the U.S.; Concerned That Silver Prices Will Rise Again 75

(New York): It is reported that the gold shipped to New York yesterday was worth a total of $11,700,000, with $6,900,000 from Britain, $3,100,000 from France, $900,000 from the Netherlands, and $800,000 from India. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

(London): Financiers are now paying close attention to the inflow of gold to the United States, being concerned that silver prices will rise again. Up to September 21, gold shipped to the United States was estimated to be worth £30,000,000. Since then, all gold shipped to the U.S. has increased greatly, so the amount of silver that must be purchased under the Silver Purchase Act will naturally increase accordingly. Although the United States has already purchased 500,000,000 ounces of silver, the amount of silver needed by the U.S. Treasury under the Silver Purchase Act has only decreased by 71,000,000 ounces due to the recent increase in gold reserves. The Treasury still needs to acquire 1,251,000,000 ounces of silver to meet the gold-silver ratio stipulated by the Silver Purchase Act. Furthermore, the only way for the U.S. to prevent the depreciation of the British pound against the U.S. dollar is to purchase silver. This is why the price the U.S. is willing to pay for silver has risen from August to 31.25. Financiers believe that once the Italo-Abyssinian crisis is resolved, the current cause of rising silver prices will change. They hope speculators will not forget the lessons learned in August. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

Chicago: Speaking at the American Metallurgical Society meeting here today, Chairman Bronwell said that the future of silver is brighter than at any time in the past fifteen years. The basic intention of the Silver Purchase Act is not, as some people say, to immediately buy up the full amount and push the price of silver to $1.29 per ounce. Such a move would quickly exhaust America's purchasing power, and ultimately, silver prices would inevitably plummet. The future of silver should be viewed with a long-term perspective, depending on whether the use of silver coins expands when the world's monetary system stabilizes in the future. The chairman mentioned the plight of countries such as China and Mexico due to the U.S. silver purchase policy, and said that what is needed now is a stable price that encourages rather than destroys the use of silver coins. He opposes further raising the world silver price. He believes that silver should be fixed at a price of around 60 cents per ounce. Because too high silver price will reduce the use of silver in industry, and silver price too low below 60 cents, will not be appropriate because it has risen and then fall. In short, the stability of the two prices is extremely important to the future of silver. Although he is not opposed to raising the domestic silver price, why should the United States pay the high price of $1.29 when most of the silver it needs can be purchased at a cost of around 60 cents? At the same time, Senator Wheeler also expressed his opinion, opposing the Treasury's silver purchase policy, saying that the world silver price could be raised to $1.29 per ounce. (Reuters Telegram, 24th)

U.S. Secretary of War Departs for Manila 76

Oakland: Secretary of War Dern will depart for Manila tomorrow. Today, he announced that the Navy Department has exchanged the large airship base in Sunnyvale, California, with the Army Department's airfield in San Diego. Dern said that this move suggests that the Army Department may use the Sunnyvale airfield as the center of its aviation activities on the Pacific coast in the future. (National Telegram, 24th)

Chinese Minister Liu Hosts Farewell Dinner for German Far East Study Group; Two Groups Will Soon Come to China 77

(Berlin): Liu Chongjie, the Chinese Minister to Germany, hosted a banquet to welcome two German survey groups sent to the Far East to study economic and commercial conditions, and the German Consul General in Shanghai, Kliebur. The survey groups will soon depart for China. One is dispatched by the German government, and its members are Dr. Tipt, Plenipotentiary Envoy, Dr. Nol of the German Foreign Office, and Dr. Rosenbruh of the German National Bank. The other survey group is sent by the German Association for the Study of China, and its members are the Secretary-General of the Association, Stellu, and Rattmann of the German National Railways. About 30 guests attended the banquet, including representatives from various ministries, railway authorities, banks, industries, education, and the commercial sector. (National Telegram, 25th)

U.S. Far East Economic Survey Group Corrects Three Points of Forbes' Recommendations for Sino-American Trade 78

(New York): The chairman of the U.S. economic survey group, Forbes, which recently returned from studying the Far East, today suggested correcting three shortcomings in Sino-American trade: (1) Establish a bank in China with sufficient capital and authority to conduct large-scale financial operations. (2) Establish a commercial credit institution that can provide long-term loans to Chinese merchants. (3) Improve the system of commercial representation of American companies in China. It is understood that the survey group's report on studying the Far East will also clearly state these three points. (National Telegram, 24th)

Wei Jung-loh's Death is Ruled a Suicide 79

(New York): Shanghai banker Wei Jung-loh disappeared here, and his body was found in the East River. Detectives have now found a woman's business card in his pocket, but the woman's whereabouts have not yet been determined and are being searched for in the hope of obtaining clues to this strange case. Today, during the autopsy, the police also found $1.10 in cash, leading people to suspect that he committed suicide due to poverty. (National Telegram, 23rd)

It is learned that Mr. Wei was born in Hong Kong, graduated from the University of Hong Kong, and obtained the Emperor's Scholarship. In tennis, he partnered with Wu Shih-kuang and won the Hong Kong Open Senior Doubles Championship. His father was Wei Pao-shan, who stayed in England for many years, and was later knighted by the British Emperor. To this day, people in Guangdong still praise his great achievements. The Wei surname originated in Zhongshan County, Guangdong, where about 130 members of the clan reside. Overseas Chinese and those in South America, Xiangshan [Zhongshan], Japan, and England, especially Cantonese people in Hong Kong, know the name of Jung-loh very well.

Impressions of a Southern Trip 103

— Special Correspondent Qian of This Newspaper

Hua

(40) Visiting the Rural Construction Pilot Zone. On the morning of the 20th, the reporter took a car to Shatang to visit the rural construction pilot zone of the Guangxi Provincial Economic Commission. Shatang is over fifty li from Liuzhou, and the journey takes half an hour by car. The director of the pilot zone, Wu Tingyang, was not present and was received by the secretary, who described the establishment process and organizational situation. It is said that the area was established in March of the 21st year of the Republic and was initially called the Guangxi Reclamation and Water Conservancy Pilot Zone. It was renamed to its current name in July of the 23rd year. The province allocates an annual budget of 20,000 yuan. The total area of the zone is 2,600 square li, making it the largest state-run farm in the province. It is entirely a pilot research institution, and after it achieves success, it will be promoted throughout the province. The goal of the rural construction pilot zone is to improve the lives of farmers and strengthen rural organizations to realize the rural society of the Three Principles of the People. Its implementation guidelines are: (1) Regarding life organization, emphasis is placed on the economic organization movement of cooperatives, establishing three systems: agricultural credit unions, agricultural finance, and various cooperative enterprises. (3) Regarding education, emphasis is placed on the integration of school and education, rural gatherings, and the training of rural service personnel suitable for rural construction in this province. (4) Regarding village administration, the village system organization should maintain the original administrative system and regional principles, but it must be simple, accurate, and convenient for various facilities. Those already established include the Shatang Experimental Farm, which also operates the Liucheng Sugarcane Farm, and branch farms in Shibeiping and Wuyou. The Shatang, Shibeiping, and Wuyou oil factories, sugar factories, and starch factories are all related to production and development. The Shatang Credit Union, Shatang Shibeiping, Wuyou warehouses, and public stores are related to rural economic organization. In terms of education, there is the Shatang School, with one qualification being graduation from junior high school after three years of study, with tuition waived and a stipend provided. The second is young settlers, who are taught practical skills and engage in part-time farming and part-time study. Other activities include immigration and reclamation. Since the 13th year of the Republic, over 2,500 surplus people from Weiyong, Cenbei, and other counties have been relocated to Shatang, Shibeiping, Shapu, Liuzhou, Wuyou, and other places to engage in reclamation, opening up more than 20,000 mu of farmland. Initially, machines were used to cultivate the wasteland, and then national manpower and animal power were used, with each able-bodied man being given 20 mu of land as a standard. Young women are also included in the ranks of able-bodied men. Settler families are provided with housing by this office, as well as all farming implements. Each family is loaned one to several head of cattle. The harvest of the settlers is divided into three and seven, with three parts going to the public and seven parts being used for their living expenses. Later, I accompanied them to visit the offices and other places. The Shatang Public Store and warehouse are located on the lower level of the experimental area office. I also took a car to travel through the fields and reached the improved sugarcane farm. The sugarcane was already taller than people, and the green leaves waved in the wind. It was boundless. A certain gentleman pointed out and explained, "This is the local variety, this is the improved variety, and this is the Taiwan variety." The local variety has thin and short stems, the improved variety is thicker and longer, and the Taiwan variety is the best. It is said that the first year of trial planting resulted in the local farmers' planting being better than the improved variety. It was said that theory is not as good as experience. The following year, the improved variety was far superior to the local variety. This year, the local variety is even smaller, and the villagers began to admire that experience is not as good as theory. Along the way, male and female settlers worked diligently, and shepherds chased after each other for fun. They were all happy and contented and could be said to have gained natural pleasure in their diligence. I also visited the houses where the settlers lived. The ten walls of mud and grass and the architecture were extremely simple. Each house was inhabited by two to four families, but they were still clean. Each family had a small living room, with a statue of Guan Gong for worship. The women were busy nursing and cleaning. After walking another li, I reached Shatang School. Some of the buildings were not yet completed, and the appearance was very grand. The interior classrooms and auditoriums were well-lit and could accommodate dozens of people. Students in the national elementary school were in class, using a small teacher system, which was very effective. Next to the school are the small villas donated by Li Baihuang and the late Ye Qi, with each house costing from 5,000 to 10,000 yuan to build. They were built to promote the idea of urban people going to live in the new countryside. In fact, other than occasionally visiting, Li and others have never lived there, so they are now the residences of school teachers. A certain gentleman firmly invited me to visit the sugar factory, oil factory, starch factory, and other production facilities. Due to lack of time, I declined and returned to Lequn Society at about ten o'clock and departed for Guilin by car at eleven o'clock.

(41) Yangshuo's Scenery is the Best in Guilin

The highway from Liuzhou to Guilin is 540 li. The car crossed the river seven times, passing through Luorong, Luzhai, Liujiang, Xiuren, Sanjiang, Lipu, Maling, Yangshuo, and Liangfeng before reaching Guilin. At 3:00 PM, we had lunch at Lipu Station. Lipu is famous for its taro, with large ones weighing several pounds. After passing Lipu, the mountains seen along the way were all isolated peaks, not connected to each other. The scenery seemed to be near Longzhou. An hour after leaving Lipu, after the last ferry, we reached Yangshuo. From the ferry, looking at the mountains in the distance, they were vaguely shrouded in clouds. The tops of the mountains were twisted and turned like knife mountains and sword forests. Nearby, isolated peaks stood tall, like islands scattered in the sea, protruding from the water. The trees were uneven, and the village houses were half-visible, resembling a wonderful Chinese painting. I hurriedly got out of the car to take more than a dozen photos. After crossing the river, I specially instructed the driver to drive slowly. The scenery became more and more bizarre, and the mountains became more and more numerous. Some stood side by side like ox horns, some towered like pagodas, some were hollow like city gates, some stood sideways like flying swallows, and some were uniquely indescribable. The car traveled through the mountains, and I was excited by the strange scenery. It is said that the landscape of Guilin is the best in the world, and the scenery of Yangshuo is the best in Guilin, which is certainly not an exaggeration. The mountains of Yangshuo have a wonderful natural beauty. They have not been artificially constructed. The mountains have more rocks than soil, making it difficult to grow forests. The tall ridges are steep and dangerous, making them impossible to climb, so there are also few buildings. Nature only provides paintings to embellish the scenery. The mountain itself cannot provide tourists with a place to climb and enjoy the scenery. Approaching the county seat of Yangshuo, pavilions were built on the mountainside, which made it feel even more precious and rare. Leaving Yangshuo, the strange mountains were still in sight, but they were not as surrounded by the mountains of Yangshuo. The highway was also less winding. After seeing it frequently, it turned to feel plain. At half past six, we reached Liangfeng. The Cen Xilin Park was there, but the twilight was vast, and we did not stop to visit. After driving for about an hour from Liangfeng, we reached Guilin. We stayed at the Binhu Hotel prepared by the reception office. Guilin was established as Guilin Xiang County during the Qin Dynasty. During the Han, Jin, Southern Dynasties, and Sui Dynasties, it was called Shian County. It remained so during the early Tang Dynasty. In the 8th year of Zhiguan, it was renamed Lingui County and served as the seat of Guizhou Prefecture. The Five Dynasties, Song, and Yuan Dynasties followed suit. During the Ming Dynasty, Guilin Prefecture was the seat of the Guangxi Province. The Qing Dynasty followed this pattern. Scholars gathered here for the imperial examinations. The mountains and rivers were beautiful, and talents emerged in large numbers. Even today, the academies stand tall. The prosperity of culture has not diminished. Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, and Ma Junwu are all from Guilin, so it is the center of the cultural area of the entire province. That evening, I took a short tour of the city. Merchants gathered, the roads were wide, and the bustling areas were brightly lit, resembling a miniature version of Beiping. The new buildings are emerging, but they have not been able to hide the feudal colors of the old days.

Prelude to Sino-Japanese Economic Cooperation: The Hebei Cotton Industry Unification and Improvement Association Guiding Planting Techniques, This Year Hebei Cotton Production Increased by Another 170,000 Dan 104

In the midst of the Sino-Japanese economic cooperation, the cotton industry issue in Hebei Province is quite important. Japan has been using a lot of Chinese cotton in recent years, so unifying the authority of the Hebei cotton industry is especially important. The Hebei Provincial Cotton Industry Improvement Association held its first board meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday at the Beiping Banking Association in Xipi City. The attendees included Chairman Zhou Zuomin (Beiping Banking Association), Directors Zhang Yuanshan (Economic Commission Cotton Control Committee), Gu Tong (Beining Railway Bureau), Tang Chengbo (Tianjin Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry), Lv Xian (Hebei Construction Department), and Yuan Songzhou (Hebei Cotton Industry Improvement Institute), a total of six people. Chairman Zhou Zuomin presided over the meeting, and the following important cases were resolved: (1) Approved the office rules of the General Affairs Department and Technical Department of the Board of Directors; (2) Approved the guidelines for promoting the cotton industry and supervising improved seeds; (3) Approved the methods for improving cotton production; (4) Purchased 300 shi of long-staple cotton seeds (Chinese seeds) to promote cotton production; (5) Decided to take over various cotton industry organizations in Hebei Province next month, and the Association will implement supervision and guidance; (6) Planned to allocate the Association's funds, to be borne by various group members. According to Association Director Lv Weidan, Hebei Province is an important cotton-producing area. There are many improved cotton industry organizations within the province, and their authority is not unified. Therefore, the central and local governments have jointly organized this Association to standardize them. Zhou Zuomin has been elected as the chairman. The Association plans to send personnel to take over the Hebei Cotton Industry Improvement Institute, the North China Agricultural Improvement Society established by the Cotton Control Committee of the Economic Commission, and the cotton industry improvement organizations established by the Ministry of Industry, the Beining Railway Bureau, and private individuals next month. Except that the funds will still be allocated by their original affiliated organizations, the design of their cotton seed experiments and other technologies will be approved and implemented by the Association starting next year. All will directly receive the supervision and command of the Association. At the same time, the Association will take overall responsibility for promoting cotton production, cotton field water conservancy, and improving transportation and sales in Hebei Province. The detailed rules of the General Affairs Department and Technical Department of the Board of Directors have been approved today. The General Affairs Department is divided into documents, general affairs, and accounting. The Technical Department is divided into survey, experiment, and design. They will be published after being sorted out. The second Board of Directors meeting will be held in a few days. Before the Association's headquarters is located, it will temporarily work at the address of the Ping Bank Association.

In the 21st year of the Republic, Hebei cotton fields were only 5,143,000 mu. In the 22nd year of the Republic, they increased to over 6 million mu. In the 23rd year of the Republic, they increased to over 7,800,000 mu (accounting for 17% of the total cotton fields in the country). According to a survey by the Tianjin Commodity Inspection Bureau, cotton fields have increased by another 200,000 mu this year. As cotton fields have increased, cotton production has also increased accordingly. In the 21st year of the Republic, its production was about 1.2 million dan. In the 22nd year of the Republic, it was over 1.4 million dan. In the 23rd year of the Republic, it was over 2.8 million dan (accounting for 25% of the national production). It is estimated that this year, it will increase by another 170,000 dan. Originally, Jiangsu and Hubei were the leaders in domestic cotton production, followed by Hebei and Shandong provinces. Judging from the situation in recent years, Hebei's production has exceeded Shandong Province and is second only to Jiangsu and Hubei. However, the area of cotton fields in Hebei now only accounts for 6% of the province's arable land, and there is much room for development. Increasing production by two or even three times will not be difficult. (24th)

The Pinghan Railway Implements a Seven-Year Rehabilitation Plan with an Investment of 20 Million, to be Completed in Five Phases, Construction of a New Railway Bridge over the Yellow River This Year 105

The Pinghan Railway Administration believes that the railway has suffered from military influences in the past decade, the tracks have been poorly maintained, and there is a shortage of vehicles. As a result, the railway's revenue has been in short supply and its debts have increased. In order to effectively reorganize it, a number of experts were gathered to study it in detail and determine a seven-year rehabilitation plan. It has been submitted to the Ministry of Railways and forwarded to the Executive Yuan for approval. The instructions have recently arrived in Hankou. The content of the plan is divided into four items: engineering, machinery, transportation, and finance. It will be implemented in five phases over seven years, with a total budget of 22,220,000 yuan. Regarding engineering, 500,000 sleepers will be replaced annually, 5,500 tons of steel rails will be purchased, 70 sets of turnout sleepers will be replaced at each station, and 70 turnouts will be purchased. All bridges along the railway, except for the Xinle Fengcun Bridge, which must be rebuilt, will be handled in stages and sections according to the urgency of the situation, including (1) Hankou to Xinyang, (2) Xinyang to Yancheng, (3) Yancheng to the south bank of the Yellow River, (4) Shijiazhuang to Beiping, (5) North bank of the Yellow River to Shijiazhuang. What is particularly important is the Yellow River Iron Bridge, which has long exceeded its insurance period. The river is turbulent and dangerous situations often occur. It is estimated that the cost of rebuilding will be 7,500,000 yuan. Important designs, such as the location of the new bridge, the length of the span, the type of bridge piers, and the type of steel beams, have all been stipulated. Construction will begin in the 25th year and is limited to five years. Regarding the mechanical aspects, no locomotives or vehicles have been purchased since the 12th year of the Republic, and parts are also lacking. Most of the vehicles were repaired temporarily to address the emergency. Often, the parts of two or three locomotives were combined into one. It is now planned to purchase 20 locomotives, to be purchased during the peak months of this year. Furthermore, the equipment of the factories will be expanded. It is planned to install the latest steam engines and generators, as well as various special-purpose machines, in the Pinghan factories to produce more parts to meet the needs. Other locomotive sheds will also be equipped with steam engines and boilers, and various special-purpose machines for overhaul will be installed to manufacture parts themselves, so that they will no longer be dependent on the factories. Regarding transportation, it is necessary to seek rapid turnover of operations and flexible vehicle scheduling. Long-distance shunting telephones have been installed between Hankou and Zhengzhou, and their effectiveness is quite obvious. It is planned to complete the line between Zhengzhou and Beiping in the short term so that trains can be centrally dispatched. The traffic lanes at the major stations and the shunting and loading lanes will be divided. All small stations will increase delays. Many stations have not yet been equipped with outer Huai station signals. It is planned to install them one by one, and to add departure signals and distant signals where necessary. The signals and turnouts will be locked to avoid personnel negligence and prevent traffic accidents. Regarding finance, one is to increase railway property. The reorganization funds for the above-mentioned locomotives and two or three items amount to 2.2 million yuan. If loans are used, not only will interest be borne, but it will be like drinking poison to quench thirst, and it will be difficult to borrow this huge amount of money until the railway's credibility is restored. Expenses should be reduced from its own financial resources. The second is to reorganize old debts. The railway administration owes a total of 91 million yuan in domestic and foreign debts, and a reorganization principle has been determined separately for implementation. (21st)

Six Agreed-Upon Measures for Agricultural Technical Cooperation Between Guizhou Province and the Central Government 106

Nanning Dispatch: The Guizhou Provincial Government, recognizing the urgent need for agricultural improvement in the province, has decided to formulate six measures for agricultural technical cooperation with the Central Agricultural Experiment Station. These measures have been entrusted to Lu Shou-geng and Ma Bao-zhi, specialists dispatched by the Station to Guizhou for investigation, to take to Nanjing for negotiation and implementation. The details of these measures are as follows: (1) The Central Agricultural Experiment Station is requested to regularly send personnel to Guizhou to guide the improvement of important crops such as rice, cotton, flax, and sugarcane, for a period of six years. One person will be sent every six months, with a three-year rotation. In the fourth, fifth, and sixth years, personnel will be dispatched in the same order as in the first, second, and third rotations, with each person coming to Guizhou twice during the six years. The travel expenses, board, lodging, and travel costs of the dispatched personnel will be provided by Guizhou, while their salaries will continue to be paid by the Central Agricultural Experiment Station. (2) The Central Agricultural Experiment Station is requested to research important agricultural issues for Guizhou Province and, when necessary, send experts to Guizhou for guidance. Their travel expenses and accommodation costs in Guizhou will be provided by Guizhou. (3) The Central Agricultural Experiment Station is requested to send experts to Guangxi University each year to teach agricultural courses. The types of courses and teaching hours will be directly agreed upon by Guangxi University and the Central Agricultural Experiment Station. (4) An agricultural lecture series will be held once every winter, with the personnel stationed in Guizhou by the Central Agricultural Experiment Station and senior agricultural personnel from Guizhou Province formulating the lecture schedule and inviting agricultural personnel from the province and senior students from Guangxi University to attend and study. (5) The Central Agricultural Experiment Station will provide opportunities for agricultural personnel from Guizhou Province or senior students from Guangxi University to intern at the Central Agricultural Experiment Station each year, taking advantage of the opportunities provided by the agricultural personnel sent to Guizhou Province. The Central Agricultural Experiment Station will also accept approximately three to five trainees each year to stay at the Station for training. Upon completion of the training, they will return to Guizhou to serve. (6) The Central Agricultural Experiment Station will introduce or purchase improved seeds on behalf of the province. Any new seeds collected that are deemed relevant to the agriculture of Guizhou Province will be sent to the province as a sample. The above six measures were agreed upon by the Guizhou Provincial Government and the two specialists Lu and Ma. It is also reported that the Guizhou Provincial Government has appointed Ma Bao-zhi as the agricultural advisor to the province.

Songjiang: Villagers of Baijia Village Robbed

Yang Guai-quan's home, a villager from the fourth household, tenth Jia, second Bao, Thirty-first Tu of Baijia Village, Tinglin, Punan, was invaded at 2:00 AM on the 23rd by sixteen robbers speaking in mixed dialects. Each was armed with a pistol and other weapons. They entered through the side door, preventing the homeowner from raising an alarm. They ransacked the house and fled after about an hour, firing two shots as a warning. Upon hearing the noise, villagers knew it was a robbery and beat gongs to gather a crowd and pursue them, recovering the fleeing robbers at the river beach.

Shatian Bureau Closed and Handed Over

The Songjinqing Shatian Bureau, formerly located in Songyi, has recently received provincial orders to merge the Shatian Bureaus of all counties in the province into three bureaus. This county will also be merged. Another office is established in Shanghai. Yesterday, Section Chief Li and three others from the Shanghai Bureau came to pay their respects to the County Magistrate and then went to the Shatian Bureau to take over.

Suzhou: Falling from a Train Results in Death

At 2:48 AM on the 25th, when the Shanghai-Changzhou train arrived at the Suzhou station, a female passenger hurriedly disembarked before the train had come to a complete stop. Due to the crowded conditions, she was pushed from the platform and fell onto the tracks, where the wheels injured her waist. Rescued by railway police, she was still able to speak, identifying herself as Zhang Fan, 60 years old, residing at No. 14, Lane 180, Wangjia Residence, Hanqiao Jiaonan Street, Zhabei, Shanghai. She stated that she was traveling from Shanghai to Suzhou to return to her ancestral home in Zhujiaqiao, Huangniqiao. She then succumbed to her injuries and died. At 5:00 PM, the local court arrived to examine the body. The station has notified the family in Shanghai.

Widening of the City Market Falls Short

The Wuxian Construction Bureau has been widening the east-west central market of Jinmen for four months since work began. The road surface work has been completed. However, regarding the sidewalks on both sides, the Construction Bureau advocated paving with concrete, while merchants insisted that the east-west central market is the busiest area of Suzhou, and the impression it makes depends on paving with cement. The Construction Bureau claimed that paving with cement would be very expensive, requiring more than 20,000 yuan, and instructed the shops to raise the money themselves. Therefore, the shops expressed deep dissatisfaction and unanimously contested the decision. No resolution has been reached to date. As a result, the central market project has fallen short. Currently, more than 300 shops in the east-west central market have jointly elected Rong Faqin as their representative to appeal to the authorities, further requesting that the method of widening Hulong Street be followed, with the government issuing 30 yuan per building as compensation for land value loss. Chairman Cheng of the County Chamber of Commerce is now mediating.

Wuxi: Three Newspapers Convicted of Libel

The Ren, Dao, and Xinmin three newspapers of this county were previously sued for libel for publishing a murder case in Caoqiao. The Wuxi court summoned both plaintiff and defendant for court hearings, and the arguments have concluded. Yesterday, Judge Liu Bingzhen announced the verdict, stating: "In the case of Xu Xiyin, Ji Xilin, Xiao Yun, and Yun continuing to disseminate libelous writings, each is fined 10 yuan, with a two-year suspended sentence. If the fine is enforced and they are unable to pay, they will serve one day of labor service for each yuan. Xu Xiyin, Ji Xilin, and Qian Xiaoyun shall jointly publish the verdict in the Ren Bao, Guomin Dao Bao, and Xinmin Bao of this county for three days and bear the costs thereof." The three newspapers, being convicted, have indicated their dissatisfaction and intend to appeal to the Jiangsu High Court.

Yangzhou: County Appoints Anti-Smoking Committee Members

The county government of this county, pursuant to Article 3 of the "Organizational Regulations for County Anti-Smoking Committees" issued by the Department of Civil Affairs, which states that the county anti-smoking committee shall consist of five to seven members, to be appointed by the county government from local individuals who are sincerely committed to anti-smoking and are impartial, and that the committee shall elect three standing committee members to handle daily affairs and implement resolutions, the county anti-smoking committee of this county resolved during the thirty-ninth county administration meeting yesterday to appoint Zhou Guren, Zhu Ganchen, Dai Xingyi, Zhang Jichuan, Hong Keting, Wang Jizhi, and Ruan Naigu to serve as committee members.

Eastern Township: Rats Cross River Holding Tails

In Dongliuji Village, Sima Township, eastern Jiangdu, there is a branch of the Outer River that is very deep and narrow. Suddenly, at around 5:00 AM on the 23rd, a giant rat resembling a civet cat led hundreds of rats, holding tails together, swimming north across the branch river, resembling a long snake. An elderly neighbor, Zhou Gui-fu (approximately 70 years old), who was taking a morning walk to that location, watched for a long time, observing that their order was orderly and had the appearance of a marching formation.

Zhenjiang: Banning the Mooring of Timber Rafts on the Riverbank

In the past, the Zhenjiang riverbank was a bustling hub of commerce with numerous sails gathered. As a result, the water flow slowed down, and silt accumulated, forcing the main current north, causing the sandbanks on the south bank to increase year by year, while the Liuwei Guazhou area on the north bank has collapsed over time, forming the phenomenon of a dead port today. Recently, ten gentlemen from the provincial capital have been seeking ways to dredge the port. The Construction Department is also planning to reorganize the Zhenjiang port in conjunction with the Yangtze River Reorganization Committee. However, to prevent silt from accumulating again, it seems necessary to first remove obstacles such as ships and timber rafts that have been moored on the riverbank for a long time. The Provincial Capital Construction Office has taken note of this and decided during a recent meeting to send a letter to the Construction Department to forward to the Department of Civil Affairs, ordering its subordinates to take effective measures to ban the mooring of ships and timber rafts along the riverbank to protect the port. It is reported that the official letter has been issued by the office.

Changzhou: Lake Bandits Appear, Troops Dispatched for Defense

The businesses in Xueyanqiao Township, which borders the lake in Wuyi County, have recently been concerned about the unpredictable appearances of lake bandits and the local security situation. They have specifically submitted a request to the county government for troops to be dispatched for defense. On the 24th, County Magistrate Hou ordered Zhou Decun, the captain of the Third Security Company, to dispatch troops to suppress the bandits. Captain Zhou then sent Wu Yunqing, the second platoon leader, to lead a team of two squads of soldiers to Xueyanqiao on the 26th to be stationed for defense.

Nantong: Dasheng Yarn Factory Seeks Loans

The Nantong Dasheng Yarn Factory and the Jiangjiaqiao branch factory have recently been in contact with a Tong-Shanghai banking consortium to negotiate credit loans, which are expected to come to fruition soon. The banking consortium and the Dasheng Factory have previously had dealings, with 4 million yuan in credit loans and more than 1 million yuan in advance exchange, all flowing into the Dasheng Factory's existing yarn and cloth inventory and various raw materials. Renewing the agreement should not be a problem.

Xu Zhen Inspects County Military and Police

Xu Zhen, commander of the Nantong District Security, inspected the county's security team, public security bureau police, and district security team squad leader training class at Xiaoying in the west of the city on the morning of the 21st at 8:00 AM. He instructed them to uphold military discipline, pacify the countryside, and love the people. Chief of Staff Peng Longxiang also pointed out areas for improvement.

Hangzhou: Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Extension Postponed to Tong-Yiyang

The track-laying work on the southern section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway was originally scheduled to extend to Yiyang by the end of this month. However, due to a bridge that requires some time to construct on the route from Hengfeng to Yiyang, it will be difficult to complete by the end of the month. Therefore, the opening of the Hengfeng to Yiyang section of the railway must be postponed to the beginning of next month. The engineering materials for the two major bridges at Guixi Liangjiadu have gradually arrived. Completion is expected by the end of October or the beginning of November.

Haimen: Supervisory Commissioner Visits Haimen for Inspection

Xu Zhen, administrative supervisory commissioner and security commander of Nantong District, having completed inspections in counties such as Tong, Ru, and Jing, arrived in Haimen from Tong on the morning of the 24th at 8:00 AM, accompanied by Secretary Sheng Yishan and Chief of Staff Peng Xiaochao. Leaders from all sectors gathered at the bus station to welcome him. After arriving in Haimen, Xu first went to Xinggan (Haimen Hotel) for a short rest. At 9:00 AM, he inspected the 19th Brigade of the Provincial Security Team and the Public Security Bureau police at the public sports field. In the afternoon, he personally inspected county administration. On the afternoon of the 25th, he went to Sanjiang Township and inspected the Second Brigade of the Industrial Security Team. On the 26th, he went to Qidong, and on the 28th, he went to Chongming. After completing the inspections, he will begin to formulate policy guidelines. During this trip by Commissioner Xu to various counties in the district, banquets were refused, and meals were prepared entirely on his own.

Local News

Xu Shiying Returned to Shanghai Yesterday: Discusses Surveying Disaster Conditions in Northern Jiangsu; Pi, Tong, Pei, and Feng Counties Suffered the Most; Diverting the Yellow River into the Sea Still Awaits Discussion of Methods; Jiangsu Provincial Government Decides on Three-Phase Relief Measures 107

A Central News Agency report: Xu Shiying, chairman of the Relief Commission, recently went to Nanjing and then to Northern Jiangsu to inspect the flood situation in various counties. He returned to Shanghai by express train on the night of the 23rd and, upon arriving yesterday morning, immediately consulted with those responsible for raising funds for the water disaster relief associations in Shanghai to discuss continuing fundraising methods and investigating the distribution of relief funds and materials. A Central News Agency reporter visited Mr. Xu at the water disaster relief association yesterday afternoon. According to his account, the inspection and relief measures are as follows:

The Flood Situation in Northern Jiangsu Is Still Not Optimistic

According to Mr. Xu, after leaving Shanghai, I made a brief stop in Nanjing and then went to Northern Jiangsu to inspect the flood situation. The cause of this flood was the rise of the Yellow River, which failed to be blocked in Shandong, resulting in it entering the Grand Canal and Bulao River via Weishan Lake. Wherever it passed, it caused flooding. Therefore, the disaster in Northern Jiangsu will not end until the breach in Shandong is blocked. The floodwaters are now receding, but without proper follow-up measures, optimism is still not possible.

Pi, Tong, Pei, and Feng Suffered the Most

Fortunately, this flood occurred in the autumn, and most agricultural products were already ripe and harvested quickly, minimizing the impact. However, property losses were still significant. If the floodwaters do not recede quickly, it will be difficult to plant new crops, and a spring famine next year is unavoidable. The affected areas include the four counties of Pi, Tong, Pei, and Feng, with Pi County being the worst affected, almost eighty to ninety percent of which was submerged.

Diverting the Yellow River into the Sea Is Being Planned

The disaster in Northern Jiangsu is truly not small. The fact that the disaster was relatively light in some areas is due to the effective cooperation between officials and people in Jiangsu Province. The current relief method is to divert the waters of the Yellow River into the Liutang River to the sea and to build up the dikes. I have exchanged views with Chairman Chen Guofu of Jiangsu Province on diverting the river water into the Liutang River, and we are both paying close attention to this matter. As soon as a plan is developed, we will begin implementation to prevent Northern Jiangsu from suffering from river floods again.

Fundraising Continues

Since the Yellow River and Yangtze River floods occurred one after another, the Relief Commission has allocated 45,000 yuan for distribution in the affected provinces. During my trip to Northern Jiangsu, I carried 11,794 yuan for distribution. The relief associations have raised 180,000 yuan and are continuing to raise funds. The funds will be remitted to various provinces for investigation and distribution as needed.

Will Return to Nanjing to Handle Relief Affairs

Regarding the matter of civil servants deducting salaries to assist in relief, the central government has decided to implement measures, which will be put into effect soon. It is estimated that 5 million yuan can be donated in Nanjing. I will not stay in Shanghai for long and will go to Nanjing soon, as there are still unfinished matters in Nanjing that need to be handled. Therefore, I am scheduled to go to Nanjing again on the 29th and will probably return to Shanghai in early next month. In the coming days, I will individually consult with those responsible for the relief associations to discuss all progress. After I return to Shanghai next month, I will convene a meeting to discuss everything.

Relief Measures Divided into Three Phases

Regarding the disaster situation in Jiangsu Province, Cheng Jingsheng, director of the Jiangsu Province Investigation and Distribution, stated in a letter to Commissioner Xu that the details are very clear. The following is a copy of the letter: "Respected President Jinglao, I was fortunate to follow you. I am deeply grateful for your kind words. After we parted at Jianggan, I immediately proceeded to Nanzu from Shanghai to meet with Chairman Wuxing, who was coming to Nanjing. I was unable to attend the preparatory Huaihe meeting. I entrusted Director Jing Gong to deliver the 2,000 yuan relief funds for Suqian. The next afternoon, at a temporary meeting of the relief society, the relief measures for this province were discussed. Jingsheng reported on the disaster situation, announced De Yi, and described the dangerous situations I encountered. Everyone present expressed their gratitude and asked me to forward their thanks to you. I will send another letter by mail. Regarding the relief measures, we have decided to divide them into three phases. The first phase is for saving lives, providing shelter, banning the slaughter of cattle, registering disaster-stricken households, migrating people to the Huaihe area, and distributing medicine. The second phase will be implemented according to the investigation and distribution procedures of the Shanghai Relief Association, including distributing relief funds, giving out winter clothing, providing funds to return disaster victims to their farms, and organizing work relief. The third phase will be for providing loans for purchasing seeds, managing price equalization, implementing spring relief, and expanding work relief. For the second and third phases of investigation and distribution, we have specifically stipulated that the relief work will be carried out by the sub-association's relief team. An administrative commissioner will be sent to each county to check households and issue labels. The general association will invite relief experts to guide the counties. The funds allocated by the Shanghai Relief Association will be used in the name of Yi in the second phase to extend the staff to investigate half of Pi County, and the strictness of the distribution will be determined by the Yi Association. The amount of funds allocated to each county is based on Jingsheng's disaster survey report and the overall county statistics, with the distribution based on percentages. Pi County will receive 47%, Tong County 23%, Pei County 20%, and Feng County 10%. A batch of relief funds will be issued first to support the first phase of relief work. All funds directly allocated by your office will be included in the first phase for accounting. (The 3,206 yuan allocated to Pi County and stored in the provincial government has already been allocated to the county.) Although Su and Mu have slight border overflows, fortunately, only local areas were affected, and there is no immediate need for relief efforts. However, it is ultimately impossible to avoid expanding the disaster area. The 1,000 yuan for relief in Su will remain in the provincial government for allocation as needed. The receipt will be sent directly to the Shanghai office. I respectfully request your understanding. Jingsheng respectfully rises early in the morning."

French Consulate General Will Hold Memorial Service This Afternoon for French Ambassador; Mayor Wu Sent Secretary to the Consulate General to Offer Condolences; Shanghai Municipal Council Flew Flags at Half-Mast Yesterday as a Mark of Mourning 110

Following the death of French Ambassador to China, Mr. Wilden, in Nanjing at 9:00 PM on the 21st due to heart disease, the French Consulate General in Shanghai immediately flew flags at half-mast on the 24th as a mark of mourning. The consulate has scheduled a memorial service for 12:00 PM today at the church on Catholic Church Street in the French Concession. The details are as follows:

Mayor Sends Representative to Offer Condolences

Ambassador Wilden had been in China for over 30 years and had very harmonious relations with both Chinese and foreigners. Therefore, the news of Mr. Wilden's death was met with widespread mourning. Mr. Gu Weijun, the Chinese ambassador to France currently residing in Shanghai, has sent a telegram of condolence to Mrs. Wilden. Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng sent a telegram of condolence to Mrs. Wilden yesterday morning and dispatched municipal government secretary Geng Jiaji to the French Consulate General on French Avenue to visit French Consul General Bautes to offer condolences.

Memorial Service to Be Held This Afternoon

The French Consulate General has scheduled a memorial service for 11:00 AM this morning at St. Joseph's Church on Catholic Church Street to express mourning. The memorial service will be conducted in a religious style, presided over by the French Consul General in Shanghai, Mr. Bautes, who will perform the sprinkling rites. Everything will be overseen by the local French Catholic Church. The interior of the church was already decorated yesterday afternoon. The coffin will be surrounded by white gauze, with the principal celebrant in the center and guest seating on both sides. The arrangement is simple yet solemn. The surrounding area of the church will be guarded by the French police. The French Consulate General, due to the short notice, was unable to print and distribute invitations to various Chinese and foreign sectors. Therefore, yesterday, personnel from the consulate notified the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the embassies and consulates in Shanghai by telephone, as well as Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Director Yu Ming of the Foreign Affairs Office, etc., who decided to attend the memorial service in person. It is also understood that the envoys and consuls of various countries in Shanghai will also participate.

Shanghai Municipal Council Flies Flags at Half-Mast in Mourning

The Shanghai Municipal Council stated that Mr. Wilden, when he was Consul-General in Shanghai, had greatly supported local public works and the administration of the Shanghai Municipal Council, and they had a close relationship. Upon hearing of his sudden death, they expressed their deepest condolences. In addition to ordering the Municipal Council to fly flags at half-mast on the 25th of this month and sending Mr. Langmu and acting business manager Mr. Lipu to attend today's memorial service, they also sent a telegram of condolence to the French Consul General in Shanghai. The telegram stated, in essence, that they were shocked and saddened by the passing of Mr. Wilden, the French Ambassador to China and former Consul-General in Shanghai. They recalled Mr. Wilden's past dedication to the affairs of the Consulate General, the administration of the Concession, and social matters in Shanghai, and his meritorious service was deeply appreciated and beloved by people of all countries. His sudden passing has been mourned by people in Shanghai. The Shanghai Municipal Council is specially flying flags at half-mast at the Public Concession for one day as a sign of respect and sends sincere condolences to Mrs. Wilden and the French community in Shanghai.

Today is Danish National Day. The Danish Embassy in China will hold celebrations in Nanjing today. Municipal and Silk Industry Public Bonds Were Drawn Yesterday Morning; Seven Bonds Drawn for Each, Totaling 210,000 Yuan; Payments to Be Made by Bank of Communications and Other Banks Starting at the End of the Month 112

The 12th redemption of the 21st Year of the Republic of China Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Short-Term Public Bonds and the 10th redemption of the Shanghai Municipal Public Bonds were drawn yesterday morning at the Bank Association on Hong Kong Road. The details are as follows:

Long-term Lending at 10% Interest; The Bankers Association Resolved Yesterday to Be Accommodating; Interest Settlement and Renewal Procedures Will Still Follow the 4% Interest Method, Differentiating Between "Huai Tou" Accounts and "Hui Tou" Accounts 113

According to the Industrial Society, the Shanghai Bankers Association held its 48th Executive Committee meeting of the second session at its Ningbo Road headquarters at 2:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included Wang Huailian, Qian Yuansheng, Pei Yunqing, Shao Yanshan, Chen Lishan, Zhang Mengzhou, Xi Jiming, Chen Shengwu, Liu Wuqiao, Zheng Bingquan, Sheng Xiaoshan, Qin Runqing, and over ten others. The meeting was chaired by Qin Runqing, with Ge Huaiqing serving as the secretary. After formal protocol, the chairman reported on (1) the minutes of the previous meeting; (2) a letter from the Shanghai Banking Association regarding the request to promulgate specific regulations to stimulate industrial and commercial circulation and to aid industry, now forwarded by the Executive Yuan Secretariat along with a copy of the review records for consideration; and (3) various reports concerning the reserve fund.

The discussion of proposals then commenced: (1) Regarding a letter from the Shanghai National Products Factory Federation requesting long-term lending at 10% interest, and asking to settle interest and renew terms using the 4% interest method, it was resolved to handle the matter as before. (2) Regarding the approval of the draft amendments to the reserve fund charter prepared by the drafting committee, and a request for review in order to submit the draft to the next general meeting of member representatives, it was resolved to approve the draft. The meeting adjourned at around 4:00 PM.

Recognizing that the daily transfer volume of "Hua Jin" and "Hua Tou" by each member bank at the reserve fund was extremely high, and that the fund was incurring significant daily interest losses, the association decided to take steps to improve the situation. Yesterday, based on the new reserve fund charter passed by the Executive Committee, a notice was issued to all member banks stating: "Regarding the resolution passed at the 48th Executive Committee meeting of the first session on the 25th of this month, concerning the large daily transfer volume of "Hua Tou" by each bank at the reserve fund, and the substantial daily interest losses incurred, for the sake of both public and private interests, starting October 1st, any surplus "Hua Tou" deposited by banks into the reserve fund will be termed a "Hui Tou" account, and will accrue interest at a weekly rate of one percent. Any withdrawal from a "Hui Tou" account will have its interest calculated at the daily interbank rate. If banks have either excess "Hua Jin" or a shortage of "Hua Tou", they can offset each other. There is no need for separate procedures, which will help to offset the losses. This has been recorded. Please take note and comply accordingly."

The Sluggish Market Affects Shanghai's Real Estate Industry, Leading to a Significant Decline; Current Land Prices Are Only Half of What They Were During the Golden Age; Vacant Houses Increase Daily, But Most Rents Have Not Been Reduced 115

According to the Central News Agency, the real estate industry in Shanghai is suffering from the effects of a sluggish market, with transactions becoming increasingly rare and little interest in even prime properties. Despite repeated attempts by leaders in the industry to find solutions, no progress has been made. Those who own large amounts of real estate are worried and eager to sell as soon as possible. A reporter has gathered the following information from within the industry:

The Golden Age is Over: The real estate industry enjoyed a golden age from 1929 to 1931. There was fierce competition for prime properties, and prices soared. Land prices on Nanjing Road and the Bund reached over 500,000 yuan per mu. Since 1931, the market has gradually declined, and each year since 1933 has been worse than the last. Currently, while there is no standard price for land on Nanjing Road and the Bund, it is estimated that the value is only half of what it was during the industry's golden age. The main cause of this is the sluggish market, but there are other contributing factors. For example, real estate merchants often mortgage their properties to banks for loans. When they default on these loans, it leads to disputes and lawsuits. As a result, people are hesitant to invest in real estate, which further stagnates the industry and causes prices to fall.

Repeated Attempts Fail: The current state of the real estate industry has significant implications for the social economy, and the future trend is a cause for concern. Leaders in the industry have repeatedly attempted to find solutions, but without success. This spring, major real estate figures such as Gan Linsheng discussed issuing 50 million yuan in real estate circulation vouchers, but the plan failed to gain support and was abandoned. More recently, industry insiders have been discussing establishing a real estate exchange in Shanghai. This plan is currently under consideration, but it is unlikely to be approved by the government. If a real estate exchange were established, it would likely lead to speculation and instability, causing anxiety among the public and affecting the financial market.

Few Real Estate Transactions: The decline of the real estate industry cannot be ignored. The solution should not be limited to a few industry leaders pursuing their own interests by proposing schemes such as real estate circulation vouchers or real estate exchanges. Instead, experts from both China and abroad, along with government officials and knowledgeable individuals from the real estate industry, should come together to discuss solutions that benefit the entire industry. Otherwise, the industry's future will continue to worsen. Currently, there are very few transactions of large properties in Shanghai. Even small transactions are rare. This not only causes losses for property owners but also creates problems for those who rely on the industry for their livelihoods.

Rent Reduction is Only Natural: At a time when the real estate industry is declining, there are increasing calls from tenants for rent reductions. Most landlords in Shanghai still charge rents based on the prices of the real estate industry's golden age. Since land prices are now half of what they were then, rent reductions are only natural. The tenants' demands for rent reductions are due to two main factors: the decline of various industries and the overall economic recession, and the increasing number of vacant houses in the city. The increase in vacant houses is not due to a decrease in the city's population, but because property owners are building more houses because they cannot easily sell their land. This creates an oversupply, which is another symptom of the decline of the real estate industry.

Shaanxi-Chengdu Route Resumes Today, All Routes Increase Frequency 117

The Eurasia Aviation Corporation's giant No. 52 plane on the Shaanxi-Chengdu route, after flying from Shanghai to Chengdu, according to the company, was unable to fly out as scheduled because the Chengdu airport was flooded and the wheels sank into the mud. It has been changed to officially resume flying today. The company's newly revised schedule for all routes will take effect from yesterday. Details are as follows:

Resumption Today: The giant No. 52 plane on the Shaanxi-Chengdu route recently made an official test flight from Shanghai via Xi'an. After arriving in Chengdu, it experienced several days of heavy rain, and the company's Fenghuangshan Airport was still under construction and not yet completed. Many of the low-lying areas within the airport had not yet been filled in. After continuous heavy rain, there was a lot of water accumulation. When the plane arrived in Chengdu and landed, because the fuselage was extremely heavy, the wheels sank deep into the mud. The originally scheduled date for the official opening of the route yesterday was therefore blocked and unable to take off. The local company in Shanghai received the above telegram and has replied instructing that the date be changed to today.

Increased Frequency on All Routes: The company's original routes have been increased in frequency and revised schedules, which took effect yesterday. (1) The Shanghai-Xinjiang route westbound plane leaves Shanghai every Tuesday and Friday morning at 6:30 AM, passes through Nanjing at 7:45 AM, passes through Zhengzhou at 10:40 AM, and passes through Xi'an at 11:20 PM (connecting with the Shaanxi-Chengdu route, arriving in Chengdu that day), and arrives in Lanzhou at 4:30 PM. The eastbound plane leaves Lanzhou every Wednesday and Saturday morning at 8:00 AM, passes through Xi'an at 11:00 AM (connecting with the Shaanxi-Chengdu route, with a northbound plane departing from Chengdu at 8:00 AM), passes through Zhengzhou at 1:40 PM, passes through Nanjing at 4:50 PM, and arrives in Shanghai at 6:15 PM. (2) The Beijing-Guangdong route is temporarily open to Zhengzhou. The southbound plane leaves Beijing every Tuesday and Friday morning at 7:00 AM and arrives in Zhengzhou at 10:30 AM. The northbound plane leaves Zhengzhou every Thursday and Sunday morning at 8:00 AM and arrives in Beijing at 11:30 AM. (3) The Lanzhou-Baotou route northbound plane leaves Lanzhou every Tuesday and Saturday morning at 8:00 AM, passes through Ningxia at 10:00 AM, and arrives in Baotou at 12:20 PM. The southbound plane leaves Baotou every Tuesday and Friday at 12:00 PM, passes through Ningxia at 2:00 PM, and arrives in Lanzhou at 4:20 PM. (4) The Shaanxi-Chengdu route southbound plane leaves Xi'an every Tuesday and Friday afternoon at 2:00 PM, passes through Hanzhong at 3:00 PM, and arrives in Chengdu at 5:00 PM. The northbound plane leaves Chengdu every Tuesday and Saturday morning at 8:00 AM, passes through Hanzhong at 9:50 AM, and arrives in Xi'an at 11:00 AM.

Revised Fare: In order to provide preferential treatment to passengers, the company has been charging fares at a 25% discount off the original price for the past two years. The company now finds the procedure of calculating discounted fares to be cumbersome, so it has organized and revised the fares based on the actual 25% discount amount, rounding all odd numbers up to 5 yuan or 10 yuan. The new fare table also took effect yesterday. Although the fares charged are lower than the previous prices, they are slightly higher than the actual discounted fares. The company's business is very prosperous, but the equipment costs are huge, so it cannot avoid losses. After the fares are reorganized, the revenue can also be slightly increased to make up for the losses. Round-trip fares are charged at 90% of the new price. As for the previous statement that the company reduced prices, it is inaccurate.

5,000 Yuan in National Currency Found in Exported Cash on the Japanese-Bound Nagasaki Maru 118

The postal liaison ship Nagasaki Maru departed from the Huishan Wharf at 9:00 AM yesterday to Japan. All of the ship's passengers had boarded and the ship was starting to weigh anchor, sounding the third whistle in preparation for departure. A coolie on the deck was carrying a passenger's luggage on board, consisting of a box and a basket. However, the luggage was heavier than that of ordinary passengers. In the hurry before departure, the coolie placed the heavy luggage basket down, and suddenly a silver dollar fell out. This was spotted by a customs officer at the dock, who suspected that there was a case of smuggling cash out of the country. He immediately boarded the ship to search it and found 5,000 yuan of cash being secretly smuggled out of the country in the luggage. The silver was seized on the spot and taken to customs. The person who was smuggling the silver was being investigated to be fined.
