Boy Scouts General Association Orders Postponement of Sending Boy Scout Works to Beijing for Collection 171

According to the Shanghai Boy Scout Council, the Boy Scouts of China originally planned to hold an exhibition of Boy Scout works from various places during the Second National Grand Review and Jamboree to be held on National Day this year. Now, because the Grand Review and Jamboree have been rescheduled to the tenth festival of next year, the exhibition of works has also been postponed accordingly. The Boy Scouts General Association has instructed the councils of various places and the Boy Scout groups across the country to be informed. The original text is as follows: "To be informed, this association originally planned to hold an exhibition of Boy Scout works from various places during the Grand Review and Jamboree this year, and limited the delivery of the works to this association before September 15, so that they could be arranged and displayed at that time. The collection methods and product labels for the works have been inspected and issued, and orders have been issued for compliance. Now, because the National Boy Scout Grand Review and Jamboree has been rescheduled to October 10, 25, the works should be postponed for submission to the association to avoid damage due to prolonged storage. Except for determining the collection period, we will inform you separately. In addition to the order, we order you to comply."

Peiming Girls' Middle School's 10th Anniversary to Be Held on October 1st 172

Peiming Girls' Middle School on Maigen Road in this port has been established for ten years. October 1st is the school's tenth anniversary. Principal Jin Yuezhang plans to take this opportunity to celebrate and make its achievements over the past ten years public to society. At 7 pm on September 30, all teachers, students, and alumni will be gathered on the school campus to hold a tea party as a celebration. At 9 am on October 1st, a celebration ceremony will be held in the school auditorium, and Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Pan Gongzhan, Shao Shuangqiu, Chen Heqin, Liao Shicheng, and others will be invited to the school to give speeches. From 1 pm in the afternoon, a parents' meeting will be held. On the 1st, a special issue of the 10th anniversary of Peiming Girls' Middle School will be published in major newspapers. At 2 pm, there will be an achievement exhibition, divided into more than ten exhibition rooms for Chinese and English, school administration, nature, society, mathematics, handicrafts, and paintings. It is also heard that the school has prepared various types of admission tickets, which will be distributed to students' parents, alumni, social figures, and various schools.

Funeral of Professor Chen Zhuzun's Mother 173

Professor Chen Zhuzun's mother, Du Kunyuan, passed away in her hometown of Beiliu, Guangxi, on July 21. It has been reported in previous newspapers. It is now heard that Professor Chen held a memorial ceremony at home on the 13th of last month, and was buried on the 14th. The Chairman of the Guangxi Provincial Government, the Education Department, and others have all sent letters and telegrams of condolences. However, Professor Chen followed his mother's instructions, believing that the country is in distress, and did not want to disturb relatives and friends, so everything was done frugally. However, relatives and friends in the hometown all came to pay their respects because of the high age and virtues of the late Mrs. Du.

Little Men (5) (7) 174

— Originally written by Ms. Orcott of the United States, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

"Catch her, stop her, chase after Curly Head! Run fast, boys, run fast!" Don shouted, running desperately in the direction she was going, because she was Mr. Pei's favorite, so if something bad happened to her, Don was afraid that he would be finished. Ah, they didn't know how far they ran, how many hundreds of times they shouted, and how many dozens of times they gasped for breath before they caught her! The fishing rods were abandoned behind them, and their legs almost broke while chasing after the cow; each boy's face was flushed, he was out of breath, and his heart was flustered. Finally, they found poor old Buttercup in a flower garden. She was exhausted after running a long distance and came here to hide. Don tied a rope around her head and led her home, followed by a group of very serious young men, because this cow made people sad to see. Originally, she had injured her shoulder and back when she jumped over the wall, so she limped, and her eyes looked like she was angry. Her once shiny hair was covered in mud and water.

"This time you're in trouble, Don," Tao Mo said, leading the wheezing donkey back with the abused old cow.

"You can't escape either, because you were an accomplice."

"We all have a share, except for Little Bridge," Xie Ke added.

"No, he was the first to bring it up," Neda said.

"I advised you not to do this," Little Bridge shouted, almost heartbroken at the sight of poor old Buttercup.

"Old Pei will not tolerate me, I think. Oh well, I don't care," Don grumbled, his tone was hard, but he really looked worried.

"We will all intercede for you, together," Little Bridge said, and everyone else agreed, except for Tai Fei, who secretly hoped that all the punishment would fall on one sinner. Don only said, "Don't bother for me": but he never forgot that. He was always worried, even though he encountered temptation and led the children astray again.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 175

— (Middle House)

A diamond in the dark, without the grinding and polishing of stones, the radiant splendor hidden within the diamond would never be revealed. This is like the course of life, without struggling through hardships and difficulties, one will never accomplish great things.

There are many men and women in the world who could have accomplished great things but died old and insignificant because their expectations of themselves were too small.

Those who accomplish great things in the world are often not the darlings of the goddess of fortune, but rather the poor children of humble origins.

If you think your job is boring, then your feelings of aversion and boredom are enough to lead to the failure of your career; an optimistic, positive, and enthusiastic attitude is the magnet that attracts success and happiness.

Archaeologist Seeks Mother in Japan 176

— (Haiyuan, from Tokyo)

Li Zhaomu, a northern Chinese archaeologist, recently entrusted his friend in Japan, Bai Jian, to request the Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department to find his biological mother. According to Bai, Li is 30 years old and a famous Chinese archaeologist. Zhaomu is his pseudonym. His father's name is Shengduo, from Jiujiang County, Jiangxi Province. Thirty-two years ago, in the 24th year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty, he served as the envoy to Japan for two years. Later, he inspected Europe and the United States and served as the envoy to Belgium. In the early years of the Republic of China, he successively served as the Civil Administrator of Shanxi Province and the Speaker of the Senate. He is now 78 years old and lives in Shanghai for his remaining years. When he served as the envoy to Japan, he cohabited with a Japanese woman named Yokogawa Kiku, from Akita Prefecture. She was the wife of Takano Fangtaro, the brother of Dr. Takano Iwataro, a doctor of law. Her husband died in Shanghai, so she returned to Li and gave birth to a son, Zhaomu. Li was transferred to serve as the Belgian envoy and took Kiku with him. Later, they suddenly separated for some reason. Kiku returned to Japan alone, while Zhaomu stayed with his father. Since then, they have never seen each other again. In his childhood, Zhaomu was raised by a nanny and barely knew his mother. As he grew older, his father told him the secret, and he learned where he came from and began to think about finding his mother. Years ago, he entrusted a friend to search in Japan, but there was no news, and he returned in disappointment. In recent years, Zhaomu has lived at No. 201, Qiushan Street, Japanese Concession, Tianjin, and enjoys a great reputation for archaeology. His longing for his mother has become more and more intense. Bai happened to go to Japan to study archaeology, so he entrusted him with this matter again.

After Bai entrusted the matter to the police department, the police department began to investigate. At 4:00 am on the 10th of this month, there was a phone call to Bai's residence at the Sanno Hotel in Akasaka. The caller was an old woman named Okamoto Saeko, who claimed to know about Yokogawa Kiku, who had passed away in the 22nd year. Bai was greatly surprised and quickly summoned the old woman to his residence for detailed inquiry. He learned that after Kiku returned to China, she lived in Kanasugi-cho, Shiba-ku, and was able to maintain her life with the assistance of her late husband's younger brother, Takano Iwao. She died of illness on January 22, 1914, at the age of 34. After her death, Takano Iwataro took care of the funeral and was buried in Komaagome Kichijo Temple, Tosa. Many years have passed, so few people know about it.

After Bai received this unexpected report, he begged the old woman to be his guide. Together with his friend, the painter Somyung Kasuga, he went to Kichijo Temple to search. He found a broken monument lying among the moss in a corner of the cemetery. Upon closer inspection, it had the words "Takano Family Tomb" on it. He also examined the books in the temple and confirmed that the name Yokogawa Kiku was recorded. Only then did he know that the old woman's words were not false. Soon, Bai sent a telegram to Li Jun, informing him of everything. I think Li Jun must be filled with mixed emotions of sadness and joy when he receives the telegram. He will come to Japan to visit the tomb soon, but I don't know if the old man on the sea will also shed old tears and regret his infidelity when he hears this news.

Memories of Mid-Autumn Festival in Nanhu 177

— Shufan

Taking three or five companions, I set sail on Nanhu Lake, intending to discuss essays in the misty rain. How carefree! The boat woman, surnamed Luo, told about her life on the lake, and then said sadly, "With guests, I can earn four or five yuan a day, but what I suffer is often unspeakable. As for rainy and snowy days, even if I am willing to sacrifice, there is no way to do so." How has the world changed so much? We all wrung our wrists in helplessness.

I traveled to the East Pagoda, desolate in the fading light. The wind chimes did not sound, much like people after middle age, unable to talk about prosperity and decline. Behind the pagoda is the tomb of Zhu Wengzi of the Han Dynasty, renovated during the Jiajing period of the Ming Dynasty. The monument has been broken in the middle, covered with tall grass. According to the Zhejiang Tongzhi: The East Pagoda Temple is the site of Zhu Maichen's house. Was the tomb embellished by good people? I secretly thought that Maichen did not have great merits at that time. Summing up his deeds, he only knew how to climb up to wealth and power and was arrogant to weak women. Compared with Su Ji, his character is even worse. How lucky to have a mound that has been passed down to this day.

I had lunch at the Fuyu Pavilion in the lake. The eyes of everyone under the ten thousand willows are green. Thinking of tonight's Mid-Autumn Festival, how necessary is it to be in a high palace in the sky if I can have a flying cup here? The building was built by Qian Yuanying of the Five Dynasties. It has been renovated and replaced. Unfortunately, the old couplets are all lost, causing the walls of the two corridors to be unsightly, which is unbearable. After the wine was over, the woman Luo begged to visit Chan Hui Temple, so I followed her. A boat headed west, passed the Haogu Pagoda, and a storm suddenly came. Listening to the clanging sound under the short awning that covered our knees, it was also pleasing. When we arrived at the temple, the rain was still drizzling. A young nun came out to entertain us. Her worldly attire made it seem impossible to talk to her about the life of Buddhism. The temple raised more than a dozen baskets of autumn silkworms, which were feeding vigorously, disturbing the sound of the dense rain. I resigned and returned to the oar, the wind became more violent, and sweat poured down my back, wetting the oars and sculls. The boatman suffered! In the evening, we arrived at the Mist and Rain Tower. The electric lights were dim, so we looked for candles to replace them. The starlight was dim, and it was difficult to describe its ancient simplicity. The lake smoke became heavier, and the bright moon was never to be seen! So we had fun guessing riddles until late at night. On this trip, those in the same boat, Fenweng, Xueming, Shicheng, and Zhensheng, all had poems for the literary and art competition. The initiators were the Shanghai Yousheng Travel Group.

Little Xitian 178

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: The Senior Official Cherishes His Reputation, Skillfully Knocks on Doors; New Love Leaves Flesh and Blood, No Way to Visit the Sick

Ze Cheng heard that he wouldn't be coerced, but he was afraid that he really would be. So he smiled at him and said, "Alright, don't worry, I can definitely help you with this." As he said that, he stood up and shook his hand a couple of times. In Jie Fu's heart, he was overjoyed and wanted to jump, but his face remained stern without a trace of a smile. After Ze Cheng left, he fell onto the bed from afar, raising his legs high and stretching them wildly in the air. Suddenly, he heard Li Shilian laugh outside the window, "Brother Jie Bian even knows martial arts." Jie Fu jumped up, stretched his hands twice, and said with a smile towards the outside of the window, "I have rules, I must do ten minutes of stretching exercises before going to bed." Li Shilian said, "Then, please rest, let's talk again tomorrow morning." As he said that, he returned to his room, thinking in his heart, it seems that when working outside, this skill of currying favor is really indispensable. Zhang Jie Fu flattering Commissioner Lan was something he had personally witnessed, wasn't that just a hard-sell flattery? So, starting from tomorrow morning, he would also go and curry favor with Jia Duocai. Although they were old friends for many years, when it came to asking for favors, that couldn't be said, he had to act expediently. With this change of mind, he also thought of a way to start. The next day, he got up early and went specifically to the most famous Nanyuan Gate in Xi'an to buy some snow cream, perfume, exquisite handkerchiefs, scented soap, etc., tied into a large package, and returned to the hotel to deliver it to Jia Duocai. The words he wanted to say were also carefully thought out. When he arrived at the door of Jia Duocai's room, he was taken aback. He saw his face was flushed red, sitting on a chair near the door, his left hand supporting his head, his right hand pressing his leg, seemingly very angry. The leg that was about to step into the door involuntarily retracted backward. (325)

The Fragrant Mists of the Imperial Incense 179

— Original work by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

After waiting for about five or six minutes, Zhang Decai went forward again to lift the lid, letting the Empress Dowager or one of us take a handful of the chrysanthemum petals and throw them in. Then he put the lid back on the stove and waited another five minutes. This special food was cooked. Every time the lid was lifted and the chrysanthemum petals were thrown in, the Empress Dowager had to keep instructing: actually, we and Zhang De were already skilled, she really didn't need to bother so much!

The taste of the fish slices poached in chicken soup was already fresh enough. Adding the clear fragrance of the chrysanthemums made it feel even more delicious. The chrysanthemums themselves originally didn't have much flavor, but after being rendered with chicken soup and fish slices, they were also very delicious. When the Empress Dowager was happy eating, she would often eat many by themselves. We stood beside her, inhaling the aroma, but it felt very uncomfortable. Occasionally, when the Empress Dowager was merciful and told us to share what she had left over, we were overjoyed. No one was willing to be polite anymore, wishing they could swallow it all by themselves.

The Empress Dowager not only loved to use chrysanthemums as a delicious accompaniment to meals, but also loved to use them instead of soap to wash her hands. This so-called washing of hands was not because her hands were dirty, but rather just washing for fun. Every time, the old lady would pick a bud that was about to bloom from the chrysanthemums inserted in a vase or placed in a pot, tear it apart, put it in her palm, and rub it hard, rubbing until the flower leaves all turned to渣, and then discard it. But she didn't wash her hands immediately, but just opened her palms and let them dry on their own. After a while, she would wash them with warm water, but the chrysanthemum fragrance had already remained on her palms, and her skin seemed to be dyed with a light green color. (425)

The Flower Girl 180

— Gu Yixin

I once traveled lightly to Jinlu, lodging in an inn. Early in the morning, when the dream had just ended, I heard a faint, flowing sound, clamorous laughter, mixed and noisy. I found it strange. Soon, the door opened, and those who entered were flower girls: carrying bamboo baskets, their appearances pleasing, three or five in a group, rushing to the bedside, each trying to sell their fragrant flowers. I refused, but they wouldn't listen. I huddled under the covers and examined them closely. They were about fourteen or fifteen years old, their figures no taller than the flower-announcing wind. Although they wore simple clothes, it didn't diminish their charming appearance. Although their skin was dark, the traces of powder on their faces were still fresh. The girls, seeing me staring blankly, used white orchids to touch my shirt. I thought, if they act like this, how is it different from a roaming cloud goddess? So, I gave them two small silver coins and told them to leave. They pestered me again, asking for more. I showed an angry expression and loudly called for the tea server. Only then did they reluctantly leave. When I got up and finished washing, I checked the cigarettes on the table, and the remaining cigarette was already gone. So, I just let it be.

At noon, my friend Su visited me and saw the flower pinned to my shirt. He laughed and said, "Have you been surrounded by flower girls?" I asked the reason. He said: "When a lone traveler lodges here, these girls think of them as customers, and they have a tacit agreement with the tea servers, allowing them to enter the rooms directly and make a ruckus. Because this place is close to Tiger Hill and the seven realms of Shantang, the flower market is very prosperous. Families of humble backgrounds don't do needlework, so they all take selling flowers as their occupation. Although they work in the early hours of the morning, their income is enough to support a family. Little girls love to adorn themselves, with messy hair and coarse eyes, they still apply rouge and powder. However, coming and going from inns, what they see and hear, how can they forget their feelings? Therefore, scandalous stories spread among the masses. In Wuzhong, there are also foolish men who come specifically to flirt with these girls. The innkeeper is neither foolish nor deaf, so he profits from it. Recently, public security officers have been rectifying the city's appearance and paying attention to these girls, so they have already become somewhat restrained."

Yesterday, I met with my old friend Mr. Wu, and we chatted idly about the Mingxing Film Company's new sound film "Night Fragrance." He told me that the director Cheng Bugao had taken the fragrant stories of the flower girls and adapted them into this play. Hu Die, who had just returned from a tour of Europe, played the leading role. Die even played a flower girl, with a romantic and charming demeanor, deeply moving people. It is currently being shown publicly at the Xinguang Theater in this city. He invited me to go and see it. I immediately remembered my previous encounter and wrote it down here. I wonder if Hu Die's flower girl is more beautiful than the flower girl I met.

Notice to Mr. Li Liping: Received your message, inquiring about the original name of "Gray Wolf." I have forwarded the question to the author, who said that the original title is "Grey Wolf" by H.V. Armstrong, published by Barker Bookstore in England. You may want to ask the Bifaxi Bookstore on the east end of Nanjing Road in this city. Perhaps you can buy it there. Sincerely, Your Brother, Juan.

Short Story

A Wu 181

— Yi Qiu

When A Wu was seven years old, her father was working as a section chief, her mother was still healthy as usual, and her younger brother had just been born. The home was filled with an atmosphere of joy and happiness. Because A Wu was very beautiful and intelligent, her parents regarded her as the pearl in their palms, showing her extra love. Although she was already seven years old, the nanny still followed her at all times, attending to her every need.

Now A Wu is seventeen years old, just like a blooming flower, even more beautiful than before. Unfortunately, her fate has fallen into the most unfortunate and dire stage. Her father, suffering from third-stage tuberculosis, coughed and choked all day long. Her paralyzed mother lay on the rattan mat all day, moaning. There was also a nine-year-old younger sister and an eleven-year-old younger brother, constantly吵着闹着, wanting food and drink. Ah! Ten years apart, it has turned into such a tragic and unfortunate family. For the sake of her parents, younger brother, and younger sister's medicine and food, she had to take on all the responsibilities. After several considerations, she finally sacrificed everything and embarked on a path that was easier to earn money.

Every time the lights came on, A Wu would begin her work of applying rouge and powder, dressing herself up like a voluptuous and alluring flower, and being sent to a game field on the edge of West Lake to be picked by others. In this way, day after day, little by little, her secret was discovered by the people living in the same house. They all began to discuss it and started to despise her. When she walked past, they would curl their lips and curse, "Bitch! Slut! Staining the reputation of our neighbors!"

Although A Wu often heard this kind of scolding, she never dared to defend herself. She could only lower her head and let them curse and mock her. Her eyes were filled with tears of bitterness, which she could only shed to the moon outside the window when everyone was asleep.

Later, the residents, for the sake of their own reputation, moved out of this house. The landlord also learned about A Wu's profession and issued an eviction order. "Vacate the premises within a limited time!" Then the neighbors all satirized her in unison, "Ah, such a pretty young lady, turns out to be a婊子!"

The general public's criticism of A Wu is, "Selling her body every night, the most lowly woman! Should be treated with the most 冷酷 treatment!" At the same time, her father suffering from third-stage tuberculosis and her paralyzed mother were thinking, "Enduring great difficulties to serve her parents, younger brother, and younger sister, and still having to do night work, without the slightest complaint, truly a rare and precious filial daughter!"

Commercial News

Financial Market and Foreign Exchange Market: Banks Eager to Sell, Gold Prices Fortunately Maintained by Large Amounts of Capital, Briefly Reaching $900, Slightly Up $1.4 182

Yesterday, the gold market continued to prosper, breaking through the $900 mark. Banks were eager to sell, and the foreign exchange market was difficult to revive. Some parties slightly divested, strengthening then weakening. The future seems to be hovering. The half-day result was still slightly up. In the early morning, the overseas silver market in England and the United States was flat, but the local market was soft. The forward silver price in Montreal fluctuated. The exchange rate had already rebounded, and the price of raw gold in London was flat. The market was still firm because of rumors that a certain bank had purchased bullion in the after-hours dark market. The off-site preparatory trading opened at $93.4. Buyers gathered, and there was a lack of supply. Although there were few transactions, the buying trend was very strong, rising to over $98. Fuxing, Yongheng, Yu Huixiang, Yu Qing, Yong Da, Decheng, Da Fa, Fayong, etc., took advantage of the high price to sell bullion. The Central Bank's listed prices were announced: the pound was flat, the customs gold unit was unchanged, and the standard gold price was listed, still at $20.5, decreasing to around $6. After opening, it was peaceful. Banks and Sassoons were active in selling, tending to decline. However, because Mobil was settling in US dollars, it struggled a lot. Free Talk

Ah Q's Father 194

— Cao Juren

Regarding Ah Q's family background, Mr. Lu Xun, the author of The True Story of Ah Q, was vague. He only mentioned in the preface: "The disciples of Mr. Hu Shih, who have a penchant for history and textual research, may be able to find many new clues in the future." I am not claiming to have discovered any new clues today; I was not born with those two obsessions, nor am I a disciple of Mr. Hu Shih. It seems unnecessary to pretend to be learned. However, the reason for lecturing on this topic stems from my thoughts at the Huang Family Garden that day. We are indeed very familiar with Ah Q's character; seeing Zhao Taiye's living room allows us to better understand Ah Q's life. An archaeologist can imagine the life of early humans upon finding a single tooth: since we are familiar with Ah Q's personality, it is not too far-fetched to speculate about the kind of person his father might have been.

Mr. Lu Xun said that the characters in his works "often have mouths from Zhejiang, faces from Beijing, and clothes from Shanxi, forming a composite character." Ms. Su Xuelin once outlined Ah Q's features from The True Story of Ah Q:

First is cowardice. Ah Q enjoyed arguing and fighting with people, but he always assessed his opponent. He would scold those who were poor at speaking, and beat those who were weak. "When encountering the strong, he dared not resist, comforting himself with words of moderation. But if he had power, and others could do nothing to him, he would be brutal and tyrannical, acting like a despot, never being moderate in his actions."

Second is the "spiritual victory" method. When Ah Q suffered losses in a fight, he would think to himself: "I was beaten by my son after all; the world is no longer what it used to be, sons are actually beating their fathers." And with that, he would be satisfied and return as if he had won.

Third is opportunism. Ah Q originally hated the revolution. But when the tide of the Xinhai Revolution swept into Weizhuang, Ah Q, seeing how exciting it was, also became a revolutionary. But when the Fake Foreign Devil forbade him from participating in the revolution, he thought of going to the yamen to accuse the Fake Foreign Devil of treason, so that the Fake Foreign Devil would be executed along with his entire family.

Fourth are megalomania and a need for self-respect. Ah Q saw very humble people, but he looked down on everyone in Weizhuang. Even when Zhao Taiye's son entered school, Ah Q did not show respect in his mind, believing that his son would be much wealthier than him.

—The True Story of Ah Q and Lu Xun's Artistic Creation

Therefore, Ah Q's nicknames are "Obedient Subject" when he is out of power, "Slave" when he is in power, and "Pauper" or "Comprador" when he is in a foreign setting. Such a great figure of spiritual victory indeed comes from a noble Chinese family. He is a son of the Chinese nation since the Northern Song Dynasty, which I will discuss today.

In the Qing Dynasty, officials would kneel before the emperor, touch their legs, and call themselves "slaves." (In fact, Han officials were not only slaves but also slaves of slaves.) A scholar supposedly filled with "barbarian" spirit—Gu Hongming—once used scholarship to prove that human ankles were born to kneel and be slaves. But history tells us that ancient officials did not kneel or call themselves slaves. Jia Yi and Emperor Wen of Han sat and discussed the Way, and Emperor Wen leaned forward to listen when he heard something that pleased him. Since Zhao Kuangyin became emperor, he changed the old practice of sitting and discussing the Way. The emperor sat and listened to government affairs, and officials could only stand and answer. Until Zhu Yuanzhang became emperor, he revised the rules again, requiring officials to kneel on the golden palace to answer questions during court audiences. Before the Tang and Song dynasties, there were many instances in history of foolish and tyrannical emperors using harsh laws and punishments to kill loyal and good people. But rulers always valued the integrity of scholars and officials and would never insult their dignity (scholars can be killed but not humiliated). It goes without saying that wise rulers treated virtuous people with respect. Starting from the Ming Dynasty, the practice of court floggings began. If the emperor disagreed with something, he would order the guards to drag the court officials down and flog them on their buttocks, stripping them of all dignity. After the Zhengde era of the Ming Dynasty, court floggings to death became commonplace. Therefore, scholars dared not maintain any uprightness and integrity. Instead, they all went to become adopted sons or sworn disciples of Yan Song, Liu Jin, and Wei Zhongxian. If a scholar, like Ruan Da Cheng, a great writer, was willing to worship powerful eunuchs as adopted fathers, then it was certainly easy for him to call himself a slave before the emperor. In the early Qing Dynasty, an elderly official in his seventies knelt for a long time and became unconscious. The eunuch scolded him loudly and prepared to beat him with a stick. A first-rank official of the court had no choice but to endure it. From "sitting and discussing" to "standing and answering," from "standing and answering" to "kneeling and reporting," from "kneeling and reporting" to "receiving court floggings," and finally to "calling oneself a slave," this shocking progress was a major event in the study of slavery.

The above describes the special training in the slavery curriculum; there is also the general training of slaves, which is more important and widespread than special training. The imperial examination system began in the Tang Dynasty. Emperor Taizong of Tang, seeing the triumphant expressions of the newly appointed scholars, felt the pleasure of having "all the heroes in the world within my grasp." After the Northern Song Dynasty, the imperial examination system gradually became complete and meticulous. Cheng Yi knew the terrible nature of this system; he said, "The study for imperial examinations does not suffer from hindering ability, but only from seizing ambition." Indeed, ever since the Ming Dynasty used Eight-legged Essays based on the Four Books to select scholars, the ambition of scholars and officials was gradually eroded by intelligent emperors, and everyone became slaves who did not value integrity or know shame. Please take a look at Ai Nanying's preface to his examination essays. He said that because he was unwilling to end his life as a poor, unrecognized scholar, he had no choice but to endure the tribulations of the examination hall. During the examinations, he was subjected to searches, reprimands, filthy appearance, exposure to the night dew and sun, hot weather, wind, and sand, worse than a prisoner. Everyone endured this disgraceful act, which they could not tell their wives or children, and forced themselves to participate in order to gain official positions. Scholars spent the first half of their lives spinning around in this circle, becoming confused and disoriented, and quickly forgetting that they should have any dignity. In the second half of their lives, they were concerned with gains and losses and pursued profit in the world, paying even less attention to morality! The scholars of the Ming and Qing dynasties, whether they studied Neo-Confucianism, came from the imperial examinations, or indulged in poetry and wine, were all well-trained slave prototypes, earning Emperor Kangxi's derogatory comment: "None of the barbarians are good people!"

Calling oneself an "obedient subject" to foreign races began in the Southern Song Dynasty. Emperor Gaozong of Song was considered an emperor internally, but in reality, he was only a subject of the Jin state. He submitted a memorial to the Jin state, stating: "Your subject Gou—having received your grace, is permitted to guard a border region, and all future generations shall respectfully observe the duties of a subject. Should this alliance be broken, may the spirits punish us, and may we be destroyed, along with our nation." If the emperor calls himself a subject to a foreign race, then it goes without saying that the common people call themselves obedient subjects to foreign races. However, obedient subjects also had different ranks. In the Yuan Dynasty, the obedient subjects from the time of the Liao and Jin dynasties were called Han people, and those who submitted later when the Mongol army conquered Jiangnan were called Southern people. Mongols and Semu people could enjoy important political positions and rights, while Han people were one level lower and could only enjoy them with the Mongol's permission. Southern people had absolutely no opportunity to enjoy them. The only advantage that Southern people had in the Yuan Dynasty was that when Yuan soldiers were captured during the invasion of Japan, Mongols and Han people would be killed, while Southern people could save their lives, but they would be lifelong slaves overseas. The training during the Yuan Dynasty's one hundred years was very effective. When Japanese pirates ravaged the coast during the Ming Dynasty, the people hung "Obedient Subject" flags on every house along the streets when the pirates landed, allowing the pirates to freely plunder their wives, daughters, jade, and silk. This was the result of the "Obedient Subject" training. The "Obedient Subject" flag was even more effective in the Qing Dynasty. When British soldiers captured Ningbo, when the Anglo-French Allied Forces entered Beijing, and when the Three Northeastern Provinces were occupied after the defeat in the First Sino-Japanese War, "Obedient Subject" flags could be seen everywhere. During the Boxer Rebellion in the Gengzi year, there were all kinds of "Obedient Subject" flags in the Tianjin-Beijing area, with some claiming to be "Obedient Subjects of Great Britain," some claiming to be "Obedient Subjects of the United States," and some claiming to be "Obedient Subjects of Russia." This further shows that the 600 years of "Obedient Subject" training had been remarkably successful. When Li Hongzhang and Ito Hirobumi were negotiating the Treaty of Shimonoseki, Ito Hirobumi said, "When our army arrived in Fengtian, we found that the Han people were very easy to govern." See, even Ito Hirobumi praised our Chinese obedient subjects! There is slave training at the top and obedient subject training at the bottom; "slave" plus "obedient subject" is the soul of our Ah Q! Friends, let me tell you: Ah Q's father is called "Traditional Eastern Spirit."

The Suicide (3) 195

— Qiandong

"Yes," Dr. Lan responded, as if understanding, still dragging his feet.

The pastor laughed again, like a child. He put the notebook into his leather bag, and his triumphant guttural sounds echoed again in the emergency room:

"Lu Changsheng! Yes, I still remember his appearance. Long hair, long face, sunken cheeks, deep beard, and eyes like those of a dead fish, always looking up blankly. He also has the yellow skin characteristic of Chinese people."

The pastor looked at Dr. Lan, wanting to know if the other party admired his memory. He saw him lowering his head, pacing back and forth as if acknowledging it, and he called out even more happily, proudly showing that he was a remarkable person:

"I can hold the psychology of a suicide in the palm of my hand. A suicide must be a strong man, at least in spirit. And also someone with a desire to live ten times stronger than ordinary people. All such people have a series of amazing histories, because a very heavy force has tempered them into such a state, which is just like moths flying toward lamps. They all lack a Jesus to lead them, so they have gone down the wrong path. If they were to walk back from this road, they would definitely become the people most capable of repenting of the sins of humanity, because they have walked closer to the 'Day of Judgment' than we have. And at that time, he will know that life is precious, so he will use the force of a moth fluttering to repent, and he will become a faithful follower of Jesus. I have already successfully tested this theory on Lu Changsheng. When I talked about the Last Judgment, when I talked about the sins of his previous life, how frightened he was! When I talked about the resurrection of Jesus, when I talked about how honored Christians would be on Judgment Day, how fascinated he was! When he left the hospital yesterday, I deliberately gave him a dollar. I thought if I did this, I would have him in the palm of my hand forever, right here." (Waving a fist holding a handkerchief.) "He said he would come tomorrow. I believe he will come tomorrow. I want him to do anything, and he will do it. I might even tell him to go commit suicide again, and he might obey. I believe even more that he is already one of my fingers. I have a fantasy that a great man's fingers must not be just five on each hand, otherwise wouldn't his fist be as small as an ordinary person's when clenched? One dollar, only one dollar, equivalent to only twenty cents in US dollars! Dr. Lan, you must save the life of these twenty cents, we should have such fingers growing on our hands! Dr. Lan, I came down for this matter, I..."

He saw that Dr. Lan was ignoring him and had walked out. He stopped talking and glared angrily at his back. However, after a while, he also heard the ambulance coming back.

The pastor stood at the door, moving the handkerchief used to wipe his nose down a little, so that his mouth was also covered. The patient arrived, the worker pushed the stretcher, the nurse held gauze, cotton, and other things, and Dr. Lan followed behind.

The pastor trembled and squeezed the handkerchief tighter. He dared not approach the patient, but only looked at Dr. Lan's eyes from a distance, because from there he could see everything about the patient.

Dr. Lan turned his head and met the pastor's eyes. The pastor was startled.

"Pastor," Dr. Lan said with a mocking look, "this person is useless. He ate Lysol, and even his intestines are probably rotten. But come and take a look at how we can cure him?"

"No, no, Dr. Lan," the pastor shook his head tightly, covering his mouth, "Your words will never be wrong, I don't need to see."

Suburban Morning (Middle) 196

— Hu Yifan

Woo… Woo… Woo Woo…

The factory whistle can be heard faintly, signaling the first shift. Some silk-reeling women, old women, and young children in the countryside quickly swallow their last mouthful of cold rice and hurriedly pick up their small lunch baskets to go to work.

Those rushing from the side streets are all night-shift workers.

"Ah Jinzi, what's happening at the factory? Is it really true that we'll be working fewer days starting tomorrow?" Lost eyes focus on a middle-aged woman with gold teeth.

"Did someone tell you a joke? Ask Zhou from the factory. They know everything. That's what they all say." She answers with a mocking smile, pointing her finger.

"It's a disaster for the poor! A disaster for the poor!"

"We used to work five days a week, and everyone complained. Now, we barely have three days of work. What's the point of working at the factory? We're going to starve!"

"Really a disaster for the poor! A disaster for the poor!"

A chaotic chorus of voices shouts out the most painful sighs. Those unemployed men staying home to care for the children still rely on their wives' wages to survive!

"Gendi, don't cry. Your mother will bring back something good to eat."

He chews on the last mouthful of rice, clears the table, and tries to pacify his child.

Laborers and rickshaw pullers crawl out of their bungalows and thatched huts, like hungry wolves, rushing towards the city.

Only those bigwigs who make their living in the city—the nouveau riche, police officers, and foreign assistants, the Western-suit tailors, and the salesmen from foreign firms—swagger down the road.

They can't forget their trade jargon: pidgin English.

"Hello... where go?"

"Hello... go office?"

"Oh oh, yes—yes!"

The sun is about to rise above the horizon, but its silhouette is not yet visible.

The northeastern corner of the sky is covered in thick, dark clouds. It seems it won't be a sunny day after all.

Caw, caw, caw, flocks of crows fly in the sky, and bats dart back and forth in the woods.

Thus, sighs are heard everywhere in the fields:

"What terrible weather!"

"Heaven is punishing the poor!"

"Floods in the first half of the year, and in the second half..."

"Master (Note) has no eyes!"

A somber expression is revealed on the faces of all the laborers. Lost pupils stare blankly at the dim sky. A cool breeze blows on the women's headscarves.

Everyone is sweating, hanging their heads, and sighing.

Timely Amusements 197

Returning from Watching the Tide 198

— Long Zaitian

Autumn is already deep. The gloomy sky occasionally sprinkles light showers! But it is said that the more overcast the weather, the higher the tide. So, I finally hopped on the streetcar to Haining.

Although it's said that it's cool but not yet cold, I didn't prepare enough clothes for this trip. Plus, the streetcar sped along the wide asphalt road outside Qingtai Gate, and sitting against the wind, a chill seeped into my legs. It was truly quite unbearable, and I felt the desolation of autumn even more keenly.

According to the schedule, the tide wouldn't arrive until 1:20 PM. To warm up and have a place to sit, I ordered a pot of tea in the courtyard of a place called Central Tea House. It was unimaginably dilapidated and desolate. The low buildings were so dark under the dim daylight that they needed to be lit. Being there, I felt an indescribable sense of oppression! Yet, it was still the fanciest teahouse around, with deformed rattan chairs bound with wood or bamboo and glass cups covered in fingerprints... It was indeed the "center" of the area.

I couldn't help but wander around nearby. Above the lotus pond stood an antique stone archway. On both sides lived coolies. A sow, majestic as an elephant, waddled with dignity. Geese and chickens scattered in a skirmish line. Several coffins were lined up inside the gate... It evoked a strange feeling in me, and I didn't dare go any further.

The number of people going out of the city gradually increased. Some were refined-looking, twirling binoculars. I followed them.

There were five or six hundred spectators on the stone dam. There were also snake-like women with wooden-faced young men in Western clothes. But it was said that on the 18th, the entire dam would be packed with people. Today was truly a small affair.

In the distance, beneath a few hazy green hills, a white line gradually enlarged on my retina. The sound of drums, like a battle drum, pounded, accelerating everyone's pulse. At that moment, a local standing next to me told me an interesting legend:

"The tide here used to be silent. Once, Emperor Qiantang was carrying a load of salt, walking on Zhe Mountain, when the tide washed up and overturned the salt. Emperor Qiantang was furious and scolded it, 'Why didn't you warn me?' From then on, the tide would sound whenever it passed Zhe Mountain. At the same time, the water also became salty, but outside Zhe Mountain, it is still freshwater. That's because of Emperor Qiantang's load of salt."

Perhaps he had more to say, but I wasn't in the mood to listen. The mast of the first ship in front of Little Pudu swayed up and down, and snow-white waves five or six feet high swept across in unison! The magnificent spectacle of that surging torrent, besides the inner experience, is truly impossible to describe even a fraction of it in existing words. The heads of the spectators moved restlessly with the advance of the tide. Many sandboats, whose hulls were previously hidden, suddenly rose and were level with the shore.

But it was also at this time that I saw an unforgettable tragedy!

These sandboats are specifically waiting for the tide to transport goods from this shore to the other. When the tide recedes, they return from the other side, whether loaded or empty. When the tide rises, they sail from this side. They do this all year round. They get four or five cents for transporting each bag of rice and five cents for each live sheep... Precisely because they need to wait for the tide, as soon as the tide comes in, the workers on the shore rush to throw the goods to be transported—rice, cotton, soybean cakes, sheep…—onto the boat in a frenzy. This scene makes us think of the pirate life of the 18th century. And the faces of those coolies are enough to make us realize that the arhats in the Buddhist halls are not illusory statues, but their models. After exerting themselves, the muscles on their backs and shoulders contracted spasmodically, and the black hair on their chests opened and closed with the rapid breathing of their hearts... In a few minutes, the entire boat was full, and then they raised the huge sail.

At the same time, a crowd suddenly appeared—old, young, strong men and women, especially old women—carrying bags, baskets, or mats… and desperately scrambled onto the boat. They were all crowded together on the rice sacks in the shade of the sail. I had thought they were the families of the workers on the sandboats, but after talking with a merchant who was probably the boat owner, I learned that they were all passengers, paying two dimes per person to be taken to Nansha. At this moment, another strong man prostrated himself on the stone steps—because there weren't proper stone steps, just unevenly stacked stones that could barely be used as footholds—preparing to jump onto the sandboat that had already left the shore. But, it was truly tragic! A surge of the wave squeezed the boat back, and he—this strong man—became a huge meat cushion between the boat and the stone shore! At that moment, his desperate screams were like the tearing of silk! It shattered the satisfied hearts of everyone who had been watching the tide. So, the tide-watchers unconsciously gathered around. All that could be seen was a large patch of blood on his pants, his whole body desperately clutching the stone shore, his eyes fixed on his nose, like a haunting ghost! The women scattered. I don't remember what I felt at that moment, just staring blankly. But the merchant who seemed to be the boat owner was still cursing, "Why did you have to come here to die! The tide doesn't care about emotions, why were you standing on the stone shore..." He took out two "big" pots and ordered someone to buy white pepper!

The spectators, without closure, dispersed. I numbly dragged my weary legs along with them, but a cruel shadow had been added to my uneasy heart!

Really, who would have thought that such a vibrant man would end his life in such a flash? (The End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Notes

Strange Tale of Making Propaganda for a God 199

— Xing An

According to a Fuzhou dispatch reported yesterday, the provincial government recently ordered the Public Security Bureau to destroy the statues in the Qixing Nai Temple in Tongtianjing within the city and seal the temple door. The so-called Qixing Nai is said to be a goddess who can protect children, and she is worshiped by the general lower class. As a result, some people have used divine authority as a source of profit. All those who worship Qixing Nai as foster parents for their children must pay a incense fee of one yuan per person every year. There are more than 8,000 registered foster children, so they can get more than 8,000 yuan, which is pocketed by the temple directors, Mr. Lin, and others. Later, some people in the community believed that these people were using the gods to collect money and should be banned. So, this year, Mr. Lin and others came up with a strange idea, announcing to the community that Qixing Nai admired Qi Jiguang, a famous general of the Ming Dynasty, for his loyalty and martial spirit, and was willing to marry him. They also consulted with Qi Jiguang's descendants and agreed to move the wooden puppet in Qi Jiguang's ancestral hall to Tongtianjing, while Qixing Nai moved to the scripture hall. The intention was to raise the status of Qixing Nai so that they could continue to use the gods to defraud money. The community was in an uproar for a while, and everyone said that it was a desecration of Qi Gong's personality. When the matter was heard by the provincial authorities, the police of the county bureau destroyed more than 200 large and small statues in the territory and threw them into the river the other day.

This is truly an unprecedented strange tale. Mr. Lin and others, directors of the Qixing Nai Temple in Tongtianjing, actually came up with the bizarre idea of ​​forcibly marrying Qi Jiguang, a famous general of the Ming Dynasty, to a Qixing Nai of unknown origin in order to collect money by using the gods. This is not only absurd, but also extremely grotesque and ridiculous. Originally, superstitious forces are widespread among the Chinese people. The general charlatans who rely on the gods to make a living can do whatever clever tricks they can, as long as there is an opportunity to take advantage of and profit from it. It goes without saying that the gods' birthdays must be lively. If the place is not peaceful, a welcoming god parade must be held to suppress evil ghosts. Sometimes the incense burner in the temple accidentally catches fire, which means that the Lord wants to go out and patrol the territory. In these various events, the residents, who call themselves pious believers, must donate some money to show their sincerity. Thus, the charlatans' labor of running around has a price. The directors, Mr. Lin and others, of the Qixing Nai Temple can earn more than 8,000 yuan a year. If they are banned, wouldn't they be wasting a lot of money for nothing? No wonder they want to move Qi Gong's idol to Tongtianjing to raise the status of Qixing Nai in order to continue their fraudulent behavior. What is ridiculous is still the ignorance of these more than 8,000 registered foster children who worship Qixing Nai. Without their stupid actions, the charlatans, Mr. Lin and others, would have no way to use their skills. Now the provincial government has destroyed all the more than 200 large and small statues in the territory and closed its temple doors, which is indeed a gratifying thing and is extremely effective in breaking superstition. However, it is heard that the authorities in Fujian adhere to the policy of not hindering good customs and may temporarily follow local customs. Therefore, welcoming god parades, and extravagance of gods' birthdays, and even spirit writing and shamanistic dancing are not prohibited. Although this measure has its own inevitable reasons, the tricks played by the Qixing Nai Temple this time may not be caused by the authorities' excessive tolerance of superstition. Therefore, the provincial government must pay considerable attention to the bad customs in the local area in the future.

Rapid Torrent 200

— Ming

My hometown is a famous mountainous province. My hometown is a small town along the Liujiang River. This Liujiang River flows down along the mountains in a zigzag manner. Although it does not have the steepness of the Wuxia Gorges in Sichuan, the high mountains on both sides and the grotesque stone stalagmites, like the turbulent river like a waterfall, are enough to shock the boatmen.

On a day when the late spring flowers were falling, I escaped from that old and dilapidated family and took a folk boat sailing on the Liujiang River to find my vague and unknowable future upstream of the Liujiang River.

I was crouching in the six- or seven-foot-wide, ten-foot-long cabin with a feeling of terror and curiosity, like a fugitive. The boat shed from the cabin board to the top of the cabin was only two or three feet high, so I could not lift my head. One side of the cabin was carrying grain, groceries, and untanned cowhide. The cowhide exuded a foul smell evaporated by the lime and sun, making my head swell.

Page 20

After a burst of gongs, the boat moved and sailed. The boat was going upstream along the river, against the current. At first, it used oars to row the boat, and then the boat ran to the river bank to pull the cable. Under the shining of the late spring sun, the river was sparkling with golden waves. The high mountains on both sides turned green with the breath of spring. The mountains and forests were showing a lush green color. In the bushes and thorny grass of these high mountains, the cries of partridges and turtledoves were rippling, bringing a melody of spring's sadness and melancholy. The warm and unrestrained spring breeze that made people intoxicated and could ignite the emotions of parting slowly blew,夹着一些野花的香味和船夫們拉纜時哼出那被生活壓榨所發出深沉悽壯的歌聲，在我這個初出門的旅人胸中織成一種悵惘悲喜的感情。

The boat was moving very slowly because the water was rapid and there were many shoals. It took an hour to pass one shoal. After passing the shoal, the boatmen had to have a meal to fill their stomachs like machines adding coal. It was not until dusk that they reached half of the journey. In front of us, the night was slowly unfolding, and the turbulent Longmen Shoal with its crisscrossing rocks and splashing rapids.

The sky was gradually darkening, and the faces of the boatmen also darkened at the same time. The cable was also retracted, and the boatmen all returned to the boat. On their dark faces, there was a resolute and solemn attitude of fighting. Then, a dozen of them picked up bamboo poles and propped the boat forward pole by pole. The boat slowly approached the Longmen Shoal. The mountains on both sides of the shoal were very high, making the shoal even darker. The boat seemed to be driving into a deep valley. The jagged stone stalagmites rising from the shoal bed and the raging waves and flying foam from the rapids hitting the reefs showed the danger of the rivers in this natural world.

I walked out of the cabin. It was time to go up the shoal. The boatmen began to use bamboo poles to prop up the bottom of the shoal, put the bamboo poles against their shoulders, and desperately put all their energy on the bamboo poles, climbing from the bow to the stern step by step, making a "yiya yiya" sound, screaming as if they were being whipped. The boat moved forward inch by inch for a quarter of an hour. When they reached the most dangerous Longmen on the shoal, the river was only two feet wide, and on both sides were stone stalagmites and reefs, like big turtles with their backs arched. When entering Longmen, the boatmen's shouts became even more tragic. The raging waves of the rapids rushed down on the boat like a mountain, and the boatmen desperately propped the boat forward with bamboo poles against the reefs, forming a magnificent picture of humans fighting nature. However, the boat's progress was very slow, and that reef was always next to our boat. The boatmen were shouting, struggling, and resisting the power of the rapids. At this time, a boatman in the front on the left, the bamboo pole he was propping on the reef suddenly slipped, and the bamboo pole went into the air. Following that, the boatman also lost the thing he was relying on, and he shook and plunged into the river with a "bang." Just right, his head hit the reef, and his skull burst. He sank into the water silently, and a stream of blood rose with the foam. At this time, the boatmen shouted wildly. One or two of them pulled out the bamboo poles they were propping and stretched them to the side of the person in distress. Then, the boat lost its resistance and shook violently. The boat boss shouted from the stern of the boat,

"Damn it, don't let go, prop up the bamboo poles tightly, if you let go, it's over!"

The boatmen also knew that if they let go, the boat would be hit by the rapids and kiss the reef. In this way, the boat would be broken by the reef, and the boat would be finished. So, the boatmen grimaced and propped the bamboo poles against their shoulders, under the tension without tears and the pressure of nature, watching their partners bleed and drift away with the raging waves.

After two hours of struggle, the boat climbed up the Longmen Shoal. Darkness had already sealed off the shoal. The boatmen's faces were gloomy with sad tears, looking at the dangerous shoal, never seeing their comrades again. Only the sound of the raging waves hitting the reefs was like the sound of beating war drums. This sound seemed to be mixed with the tragic cries and sobs of the unfortunate person. From the dark forests and thorny grass valleys of the high mountains on both sides, there were also intermittent cries of turtledoves and partridges. This is the first picture of the tragedy of life I saw on the way to becoming a master.

Maggots 201

— Yang Zhongshuo

The place where I live is extremely quiet, with weeping willows, greenery, and a clear spring.

Not far from where I live, there is an ancient temple with a long history. The loud sound of the evening bell has awakened my dreams for several years. I have been able to break free from the shackles of reality, be content with my fate, and live this leisurely life in peace and tranquility. In the final analysis, I am still fascinated by that bell.

Because it has not been repaired for many years, this temple is showing signs of collapse. The dilapidated walls, the broken tiles, and the mottled walls all indicate that it is so old that it has been forgotten by people.

However, the antique mottled color fascinated me. Every evening, in the sound of wooden fish bells and drums, I quietly walked into this temple.

Because I come every day, the monks all recognize me. They are mostly humble and polite when we meet, and very kind.

The abbot is a middle-aged man around forty years old, with a face that is full but slightly thin. From his actions and manners, he has the qualities of a scholar. He asks me with a smiling face what I do every day when he sees me.

"Read books and practice calligraphy, nothing else," I always answer him with this sentence. But I have never seen him have the slightest expression of impatience. Sometimes he even smiles with his eyes narrowed, even though my answer is so stereotyped and has never changed.

When I first went there, everyone was a little reserved. Later, as we gradually became familiar with each other, there was no pretense in our conversations.

Once, I went to look for him again. After asking me what I did as usual, he began to tell me about his past. He said that he used to be an officer in charge of troops, a director of a tax collection office, and an active figure in the political vortex, which made me feel very surprised. How could a person who lived in an environment of wine, meat, and extravagance put down the butcher knife and break away from the prosperous reality to live this desolate life? This cannot but be considered a miracle. However, this miracle is not too strange. What is strange is: since he has become a monk, he should have his six senses purified and wholeheartedly convert to my Buddha. However, he also told me that although he had become a monk, he still drank alcohol and ate meat. When he was in the mood, he would also invite three or four friends to go to the nearby brothel to have tea.

If these words were heard by those moralists, I really don't know to what extent they would scold him. However, I found his frank and straightforward confession very cute.

I once asked him why he wanted to be a monk. He said without hesitation, and very cleverly, "If a person is buried in an environment of sensual pleasures and extravagance all his life, what is the difference between him and a maggot in a dung heap? The reason why I have the heart to leave my family and wife and regard wealth and fame as floating clouds is because I am not willing to be a maggot!"

I was moved by his remarks. I sympathized with him, admired him, and was even more deeply impressed by his brilliant insights. I almost wanted to abandon my current life immediately and hide in that unfathomable and mysterious empty door.

However, after I expressed my wishes, he opposed it again and said, "You are still young after all, and you have not tasted the stench of the dung heap thoroughly. Moreover, this era does not seem to need a passive lifestyle. The fragmentation of the country depends on you young people to sew up. The so-called reincarnation and nirvana in Buddhism are just admonitions to persuade people to do good and warn the world. You young people have not committed the crime of deceiving the world and stealing the country, nor have you done anything against your conscience, so why bother to do this? It is not in vain to be young and to be passive. I personally cannot agree, and your family and friends will not allow it!"

Recently, I have not been to that ancient temple for several days. When I am alone and bored, I will use my thoughts on those illusory images. "To be a dung maggot, or to transcend oneself?" This question often swirls in my mind.

A sudden news made me stunned. Yesterday evening, I re-entered the ancient temple in the sound of wooden fish bells and drums. But the abbot was gone. At first, I thought he had gone to the brothel with three or four friends. Later, according to another monk, he - the abbot - had been appointed by a province to be a county magistrate. After hearing the monk's words, I smiled bitterly with my mouth pursed.

From this time on, my "preconceptions" began to shake. I realized that everywhere in this world is a dung heap!

The abbot was unable to escape reality after all and still had to wriggle in the dung heap! It is still a maggot in the dung heap!

The Monkey Handler 202

— Yan

After the store across the street was demolished, the plot of rubble lay barren for more than half a year without reconstruction. Rumor had it that two leaseholders were discovered on this two-mu-plus plot, leading to unresolved litigation. Another account said the landowner lacked the capital for reconstruction, so this open space became a venue for miscellaneous entertainments.

My bedroom faces this open space diagonally. Since there were no buildings rebuilt, the view, though at an angle, was unobstructed. Returning from the company, it was just as the sun was setting in the west, which was also the busiest time for the open space. There were peep shows, boxing matches, monkey handlers, and many vendors gathering here, creating a small market. Schoolchildren returning home and lower-class women used it as their entertainment venue, and business seemed to be thriving. If, as one account said, the landowner lacked the capital to rebuild, dividing the land into sections and collecting tolls would have yielded considerable profits in half a year.

Taking advantage of my window, I would idly lean on the windowsill to watch the bustle. Because the monkey handler's performance area was closest to my view, and his circle of spectators was particularly crowded, I would inexplicably watch the monkey's antics with the same tireless fascination as those spectators. Sometimes, when I returned home a little later, they had already dispersed, and I felt a sense of lingering longing.

Humans evolved from apes, so it's not surprising that these monkeys can perform little tricks. I am no longer in the mindset of childhood, watching the monkey's jumping and finding joy in it, especially since it's always the same few tricks every day. What I couldn't forget was the monkey handler: his temples were already gray, at least in his late fifties. He was all alone, without a helper, and the monkey was probably his only companion. He beat the gong himself, greeted the audience himself, sang tuneless melodies himself, and directed the monkey to perform himself. He was hunchbacked, and under such strenuous work, he often panted, sweated, and still tried to keep his eyes on the audience, fearing they would become dissatisfied and leave. Every day, he collected money twice, bowing to each spectator, which made his figure even smaller. Whether the amount was sufficient, the two collections were full enough, I imagine, to cover his and his only companion monkey's food and lodging for the day.

But these past few days, the miscellaneous entertainment venues in the open space have dwindled, and the old monkey handler has also disappeared. I asked a child who played in the open space every day, and the child replied that he didn't know. Today, however, I encountered this pair of interdependent companions in our alley. He was still wearing that tattered, multi-layered garment, beating the gong alone. The audience was naturally not as large as when he was in the open space. As I entered the alley, he was holding the gong to collect money. I casually threw a few coins to him. He bowed habitually, mechanically like the monkey performing, feigning an awkward smile, and repeatedly thanked me in a Shandong accent.

After collecting the money, he gave a general bow and led the monkey away. I originally wanted to ask him a few questions, but seeing how laboriously he walked, I didn't dare to speak. But someone in the alley had already asked him the reason for not being in the open space these past few days. It was because someone with authority on that road demanded a toll from him, and he was driven away because he couldn't afford this unexpected expense.

Radio Broadcast Schedule

Song Introductions 203

Lotus Picking Song

Picking lotus, gently paddling the oars, slowly moving the boat, in the deep waters of the lake where the flowers are fresh. Picking, picking lotus, picking lotus, stretching arms vigorously, tilting the body, waves break and the boat rocks. Picking, picking lotus, with a shy and tearful face, the stem breaks but the thread still connects, the flower is delicate, as beautiful as a human face, the leaves are graceful, like a young man. Picking, picking lotus, I only hope that my fate is not as bitter as the lotus heart, and only hope that your heart is stronger than the lotus stem. Picking, picking lotus, the common people plant white jade lotus roots, the nobles harvest and transport them in the setting sun. Picking, picking lotus, reaching far and wide, white lotus roots are as clear as water. Picking lotus.

Page 22

Page 23

Picking lotus, paddling the boat, weaving through the waves, picking, picking lotus, picking, blowing wind drives the boat forward, raindrops pierce through the cold clothes. Picking lotus, blowing wind drives the boat forward, difficult to think of loved ones. The flower buyers don't care about wind and rain, sending fresh flowers quickly to the dressing table. Picking, picking lotus, I am willing to work hard to pick a few more flowers, only hoping that the fresh flowers can earn money to support the family. Picking, picking lotus, picking lotus in the morning, three meals are hard to fill, picking lotus in the evening, clothes are not warm enough. Picking, picking lotus, year after year exhausted by hunger and cold, every year rocking the boat at five in the morning. Picking, picking lotus.

Ballad Singing 204

Zhou Jianhong and Yu Kuilong

Oriental (1020) 11:15 AM to 12:00 PM

Opening: "Liu Yi"

Peach blossoms are like embroidery, willows are like gold. Zhang Xu invited Liu Yi to travel. Both are talented and handsome. Both are classmates and from the same hometown. They go on spring outings together to find poetic inspiration. Strolling leisurely near the seashore. They see a shepherdess with a sorrowful expression. Ashamed to be seen, startled by people. Her clothes are not like those of ordinary women. A kind of grace is wonderfully divine. Without a care, he asks the beautiful girl. Where is your family origin? The beautiful figure does not resemble a shepherd. She lowers her eyes and speaks softly in shame. Her soft voice is like an oriole coming out of a valley. I am because my father is angry. Today I earnestly ask you to deliver a message. The rhinoceros hairpin on my head can serve as proof. The large tree by the river can serve as the door. As she points and as she says. There is indeed a large tree by the river. He knocks lightly several times. Who knew that this hairpin was made of rhinoceros horn. In an instant, it can divide the sea water. Crystal palace, glass seat. He sees a crowned man on the throne. The emperor is suddenly enraged. Since it has come to this, let us be merciful. Discussing marriage is not hindered by the separation of the netherworld. Drums boom and music plays. Marrying into the dragon palace, the lord of Dongting.

News 207

The Yisheng Concert will be held today from 5:30 PM to 6:00 PM at the Jiaotong Radio Station (1300). Teaching harmonica, musical notes, new single-tone playing method. Harmonica lovers from all walks of life are welcome to listen at that time.

The General Society of the Chinese Red Cross, in view of the severe floods in various provinces, has specially organized a fundraising committee, approved by the Ministry of Interior, to engage in raising relief funds, in order to distribute them as soon as possible. And in view of the increasingly urgent world situation, in order to train rescuers and reserve rescue materials, it is even more proactive in soliciting members this year. In addition to the Level 1-5 members, there is also a supporting certificate, priced at one yuan per certificate. Soliciting compatriots across the country, each person bearing one yuan, to fund rescue work, in order to seek security guarantees for humanity. This matter is of great importance and relies entirely on the enthusiastic donations of the public. In order to expand publicity, in addition to the obligation of each radio station to report daily, a special program will be broadcast every Sunday on Foyin Radio Station. This time, on the evening of September 29th, starting at 8:15 PM, the last special program will still be broadcast on Foyin Radio Station, with speeches by Secretary-General Cao Yunxiang, Secretary Gan Shuhan, Propaganda Director Shen Jintao, and guest Ms. Xiong Saiying. We have requested Mr. Zhang Shichuan, Zhou Jianyun, and Dong Tianya to ask Film Queen Hu Die and all the male and female stars of the Star Film Company, such as Gao Zhanfei, Xu Lai, Yan Yuexian, Ye Qiuxin, Huang Naishuang, Tang Jie, Zhu Qiuhen, Gu Lanjun, and Shu Xiuwen, to broadcast the latest songs. Gu Meijun, Wang Huijuan, Jing Liting, Wang Mengshi, Tan Zhiyuan, Tang Wei, and Wang Jiting will sing Peking Opera. Foyin Radio Station originally had 500 watts, but now it has temporarily added power, so that both domestic and foreign listeners can hear it. The detailed program will be disclosed by this newspaper this Sunday.

The Yuexing Singing Society will begin broadcasting the latest songs next month and is now recruiting several female members. Those who are interested in noble songs can send a detailed resume with a personal photo to No. 8, Bailinan Branch Road, to the society.

Movie News

Lu Shi Establishes Shanghai Drama Film Research Institute 208

Lu Shi was previously hired by the Performing Arts Experimental Institute as its director. However, due to the internal reorganization of the institute, Lu Shi also announced his withdrawal. It is now reported that after Lu Shi's departure from the institute, he is now actively establishing a slightly different institution, reportedly named the "Shanghai Drama Film Research Institute." The scope will be further expanded, and famous figures will be hired as faculty members. Once the arrangements are in place, the establishment and enrollment announcement will be made in the newspaper. (Sun Yimin, 465 Dongxi Huade Road, Hongkou: The above text is a news release sent to us and does not mean that the Shanghai Drama Film Research Institute is affiliated with the Shen Bao. If you want to register, etc., please send the photos directly after it announces its establishment. This publication cannot do it for you. "Be careful, be careful," the editor respectfully replies.)
